1 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Burke v. Commonwealth


2014-SC-000472-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


506 S.W.3d 307; 2016 Ky. LEXIS 631



December 15, 2016, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 5, 2017


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2011-CA-000972-MR. KENTON CIRCUIT COURT NO. 10-CR-00563.
Burke v. Commonwealth, 2014 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1034 (Ky. Ct. App., July 18, 2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.031, on hate crime designation, was constitutional as written and applied because it mandated nothing, defendant was not entitled to pre-trial notice of the designation or a jury finding, a listed factor only had to be a crime's primary factor, and sufficient evidence showed defendant's perception of a victim's sexual orientation was a primary factor in her assault; [2]-Evidentiary rulings were not an abuse of discretion because defendant's photo showing a swastika tattoo was relevant to identity, and irrelevant drug evidence was harmless; [3]-Jury instructions did not palpably err because a second degree assault instruction did not have to include imperfect self-defense, and including a knife as a dangerous instrument or deadly weapon in a second-degree assault instruction did not err.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part.

 

2 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Goben v. Commonwealth


2014-SC-000712-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


503 S.W.3d 890; 2016 Ky. LEXIS 630



December 15, 2016, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 5, 2017


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JUDITH E. MCDONALD-BURKMAN, JUDGE. NOS. 09-CR-003648 AND 10-CR-000177.
Goben v. Commonwealth, 2015 Ky. Unpub. LEXIS 56 (Ky., Aug. 20, 2015)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Although significantly delayed by the prosecution of earlier drug charges, the delay in defendant's trial for the instant charges was not unconstitutional where the five-year delay was due to the government's prosecution of the prior offenses, the delay caused by the government's actions following the conclusion of the prior case was brief, and because defendant was already incarcerated, the two-month delay caused by the government was not prejudicial; [2]-Although the trial court exceeded slightly the Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 500.110 deadline, defendant's right to prompt disposition was not violated as the need to ensure that defendant was tried by a jury unaffected by the trial court's mistake in reading the indictment and to accommodate defense counsel's schedule made the two-month postponement and one-month breach of the statutory limit reasonable.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed and remanded to clarify sentence.

 

3 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Guernsey


2015-SC-000259-TG AND 2015-SC-000261-TG (2015-CA-000722-MR AND 2015-CA-000723-MR) AND 2015-SC-000260-TG AND 2015-SC-000262-TG (2015-CA-000722-MR AND 2015-CA-000723-MR)


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


501 S.W.3d 884; 2016 Ky. LEXIS 496



October 20, 2016, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 10, 2016.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE PAMELA GOODWINE. NOS. 13-CR-01170 AND 13-CR-01170-001.

ON APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE PAMELA GOODWINE. NOS. 13-CR-01170 AND 13-CR-01170-002.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A circuit court erred in concluding pretrial that the imposition of the death penalty would be a disproportionate penalty where, pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.075, the sole responsibility for conducting a comparative proportionality review rested with the Supreme Court of Kentucky, and the exercise of the circuit court's retained authority to determine whether a death sentence was inherently disproportionate was proper only after the Commonwealth had the opportunity to present all of its evidence in the guilt phase of trial; [2]-The Commonwealth had not forfeited the right to interlocutory review of the issue where the authority of the circuit court to exclude the death penalty prior to trial over the objection of the Commonwealth was squarely presented to the court.


OUTCOME: Order vacated; case remanded.

 

4 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth ex rel. Andy Beshear v. Matthew Bevin


2016-SC-000272-TG AND 2016-SC-000273-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


498 S.W.3d 355; 2016 Ky. LEXIS 435



September 22, 2016, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 13, 2016.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE THOMAS D. WINGATE, JUDGE. NO. 16-CI-00389. (2016-CA-000738-MR). ON APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE THOMAS D. WINGATE, JUDGE. NO. 16-CI-00389. (2016-CA-000745-MR).


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Plaintiff Attorney General had standing to contest defendant Governor's reductions of state universities' appropriated allotments because he had a cognizable interest in ensuring legal government action and defending constitutional statutes; [2]-Plaintiffs legislators had no standing because their personal stake in statutory execution was insufficient; [3]-The Governor could not reduce the allotments because his Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 48.130 authority to reduce appropriations in a budget shortfall did not apply, this exceeded his Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 48.620(1) authority to revise allotments and his Ky. Rev. Stat. § 45.253(4) authority to withhold allotments, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 164A.555 clearly required paying appropriated sums to the universities, despite any inconsistency with Ky. Rev. Stat. ch. 45, and he could not make the universities not spend appropriations.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

 

5 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Jenkins v. Commonwealth


2014-SC-000353-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


496 S.W.3d 435; 2016 Ky. LEXIS 327



August 25, 2016, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 15, 2016.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Jenkins v. Kentucky, 137 S. Ct. 1205, 197 L. Ed. 2d 250, 2017 U.S. LEXIS 1566 (U.S., Feb. 27, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM OHIO CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE RONNIE C. DORTCH, JUDGE. NO. 06-CR-00121.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant was not entitled to a directed verdict or the dismissal of the rape and sodomy charges where there was sufficient evidence of forcible compulsion under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 510.010(2) to raise a jury question, as the victim testified that defendant forcibly rolled her over, removed her pajama pants, and then physically pushed aside her several attempts to block him from sodomizing her, and defendant's acts were not actions merely incidental to sex; [2]-Defendant's sodomy conviction under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 510.070 was reversed because, while he was charged with a single count of sodomy, there was proof of two sodomies, and the trial court gave a duplicitous jury instruction that allowed the jury to convict on the basis of either one; [3]-The trial court did not err by denying defendant's request for an instruction under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 510.140.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.

 

6 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Howard v. Commonwealth


2015-SC-000377-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


496 S.W.3d 471; 2016 Ky. LEXIS 333



August 25, 2016, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 15, 2016.
Related proceeding at Lee v. Commonwealth, 2017 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 740 (Ky. Ct. App., Oct. 6, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM CARROLL CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE REBECCA LESLIE KNIGHT, JUDGE. NO. 15-CR-00005.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A trial court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing defendant where there was no proof that the court failed to consider mitigating circumstances, defendant had pled guilty after thrice being advised of the implications, the court observed proper sentencing procedures, and the sentence was based on a number of factors, including defendant's recidivism; [2]-The sentence did not violate Ky. Const. § 13 or the Fifth Amendment given prior case law holding that multiple counts of trafficking in a controlled substance did not violate double jeopardy protections; [3]-The trial court did not commit palpable error in imposing punishment given the multiple counts and his guilty plea; [4]-The trial court did not err in imposing court costs where it made no factual determination that defendant was a poor person under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23A.205; [5]-A criminal fine was vacated.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and vacated in part.

Rice v. Commonwealth


2014-SC-000733-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


492 S.W.3d 563; 2016 Ky. LEXIS 252



June 16, 2016, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 7, 2016.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS CASE. NO. 2013-CA-002045-MR. BOURBON CIRCUIT COURT NO. 12-CR-00101.
Rice v. Commonwealth, 2014 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 876 (Ky. Ct. App., Nov. 14, 2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Court of Appeals erred in finding that defendant was not eligible for home incarceration under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.210 because he pled guilty to two non-violent Class D felonies, DUI, fourth offense, and driving on a DUI-suspended license, second offense, was sentenced to an indeterminate term of imprisonment of five years or less, and, subject to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.100(4)(a), he was to serve his sentence in the county jail.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded.

 

8 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Allstate Ins. Co. v. Smith


2013-SC-000732-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


487 S.W.3d 857; 2016 Ky. LEXIS 168



May 5, 2016, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 26, 2016.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2009-CA-001961. JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT NO. 09-CI-000399.
Smith v. Allstate Ins. Co., 2010 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 719 (Ky. Ct. App., Sept. 10, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The appellate court erred in reversing the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of an insurer in the insured's breach of contract action because, while Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 304.20-020(2) mandated that a liability policy should be delivered or issued unless it contained a provision for uninsured motorists, the insurer had no duty to mention UIM except when the first renewal notice was delivered to the insured, the insurer advised the insured about UIM coverage via a form notifying the insured that he could purchase higher limits for UIM and conveyed the very information required by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 304.20-040(13), the insured's policy was clear that UIM coverage was not provided, and the insured's lengthy relationship with the insurer, standing alone, was insufficient to create an affirmative duty to notify or counsel the insured on UIM's availability.


OUTCOME: Appellate judgment reversed and trial court's judgment reinstated.

 

9 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


St. Joseph Healthcare, Inc. v. Thomas


2014-SC-000008-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


487 S.W.3d 864; 2016 Ky. LEXIS 179



May 5, 2016, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 26, 2016.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2012-CA-000941-MR. FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT NO. 000-CI-01364.
St. Joseph Healthcare, Inc. v. Thomas, 2013 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1011 (Ky. Ct. App., Dec. 6, 2013)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Punitive damages for appellant hospital's refusal to treat a patient were proper because his removal, contrary to the Emergency Medical Treatment and Active Labor Act (EMTALA), and threat of arrest showed Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 411.184(1)(a) oppression and common law gross negligence; [2]-The hospital ratified employees' acts, under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 411.184(3), because management knew what happened and threatened the patient's arrest; [3]-The hospital was liable for physicians' EMTALA violations because EMTALA's duty was nondelegable; [4]-Punitive damages over a single-digit ratio to compensatory damages did not offend due process because the hospital's offensive conduct violated EMTALA public policy, and the patient had few economic prospects; [4]-No abuse of discretion for keeping an alleged sleeping juror was shown because the record was undeveloped.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

10 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Jamgotchian v. Ky. Horse Racing Comm'n


2014-SC-000108-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


488 S.W.3d 594; 2016 Ky. LEXIS 171



May 5, 2016, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 26, 2016.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Jamgotchian v. Ky. Horse Racing Comm'n, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 7163 (U.S., Nov. 28, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2012-CA-002154-MR. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT NO. 11-CI-01047.
Jamgotchian v. Ky. Horse Racing Comm'n, 2014 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 851 (Ky. Ct. App., Feb. 7, 2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Courts could hear appellant buyer's declaratory judgment claim that regulations barring "claimed" horses' out-of-state racing violated U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3, because he was sufficiently interested, under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 418.040, in their constitutionality; [2]-The regulations were not entitled to governmental functions' lesser scrutiny because private enterprises conducted racing, despite pervasive regulation; [3]-The regulations did not violate the dormant commerce clause because their negligible protectionist effect advanced classifying racehorses, and the buyer agreed to this limited bar by seeking a claiming race's benefits instead of buying a horse in another manner, so they did not try to insulate Kentucky's race tracks from out-of-state competition; [4]-They were not impermissibly extraterritorial because they did not regulate racing in other states.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

11 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


White v. Commonwealth


2013-SC-000791-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


500 S.W.3d 208; 2016 Ky. LEXIS 169



May 5, 2016, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified by White v. Commonwealth, 2016 Ky. LEXIS 515 (Ky., May 5, 2016)
Rehearing denied by White v. Commonwealth, 2016 Ky. LEXIS 544 (Ky., Oct. 20, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM POWELL CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JOHN DAVID CAUDILL, JUDGE. NO. 79-CR-00024.
White v. Commonwealth, 671 S.W.2d 241, 1983 Ky. LEXIS 317 (Ky., 1983)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court properly found that defendant was not entitled to public funds for an expert of his choosing because nothing in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 31.185(1) required the use of private psychological evaluations to be paid for with public funds, and that determination was within the trial court's discretion; [2]-Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 532.140 and 532.130 and other relevant statuary provisions were unconstitutional to the extent that the intelligence quotient score referenced in those provisions was applied as a dispositive factor in determining whether an offender is eligible for execution; [3]-Defendant's continued failure to submit to the Kentucky Correctional Psychiatric Center's (KCPC) custody did not constitute waiver because the record reflected ample evidence that the KCPC was capable of examining and evaluating defendant.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part and case remanded.

Craft v. Commonwealth


2014-SC-000386-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


483 S.W.3d 837; 2016 Ky. LEXIS 107



March 17, 2016, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 7, 2016.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE CHARLES LOUIS CUNNINGHAM, JR., JUDGE. NO. 11-CR-000007.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's claim that trial courts' discretion to set the appropriate number of prosecutorial peremptory challenges violated separation of powers was not considered because he did not give the Attorney General notice of his constitutional argument pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 418.075; [2]-Defendant was not entitled to a directed verdict in his murder prosecution, based on an argument that a lack of eyewitness testimony made it impossible to determine his mental state at the time of the crime because sufficient evidence allowed a reasonable jury to infer the intent required by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 507.020(1) from the wound defendant caused showing he created a grave risk of death with extreme indifference to human life.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

13 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Maloney v. Commonwealth


2014-SC-000339-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


489 S.W.3d 235; 2016 Ky. LEXIS 98



March 17, 2016, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 16, 2016.
Rehearing denied by Maloney v. Commonwealth, 489 S.W.3d 235, 2016 Ky. LEXIS 288 (Ky., June 16, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2013-CA-000213-MR. MONTGOMERY CIRCUIT COURT NO. 12-CR-00168.
Maloney v. Commonwealth, 2014 Ky. App. LEXIS 101 (Ky. Ct. App., June 13, 2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The circuit court erred in denying defendant's motion to suppress because a police officer had no authority under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 431.005 to arrest defendant for alcohol intoxication in a public place, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 222.202(1), and thus, the search incident to the arrest was not valid; [2]-The offense was not committed in the presence of the officer, and defendant, who was lying flat on the floor of his front porch in a state of total repose, was doing nothing that could pose a danger to himself or others; [3]-Section 222.202(1) did require some manifest behavior that was likely to produce the requisite endangerment or annoyance, and being passed out, asleep, or otherwise unconscious on a porch did not satisfy that requirement of the statute.


OUTCOME: Judgment vacated.

 

14 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


B.H. v. Commonwealth


2013-SC-000254-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


2016 Ky. LEXIS 106



March 17, 2016, Rendered


NOTICE:

PLEASE REFER TO THE KENTUCKY RULES REGARDING FINALITY OF OPINIONS. TO BE PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified: April 13, 2016.
Substituted opinion at B.H. v. Commonwealth, 2016 Ky. LEXIS 421 (Ky., Mar. 17, 2016)
Rehearing granted by B.H. v. Commonwealth, 2016 Ky. LEXIS 413 (Ky., Aug. 25, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2012-CA-001768-DR. WOODFORD CIRCUIT COURT NO. 11-XX-00001; WOODFORD JUVENILE COURT NO. 09-J-00050-004.
B.H. v. Commonwealth, 2014 Ky. LEXIS 132 (Ky., Mar. 12, 2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The supreme court could not reach the merits of defendant juvenile's claims because there was no proper appeal before the supreme court, and no appeal below had been appropriate; [2]-The circuit court erred in considering defendant's claims because defendant waived his right to appeal since he entered into his admission under Ky. Rev. Stat. § 610.080 unconditionally and indicated that he did so knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily, with his attorney present and encouraging his plea; [3]-Although a juvenile did not enter a guilty plea, his or her admission to the allegations in the petition had much of the same effect as such a plea, and that effect included barring any appeal, other than one claiming that no offense had been charged, unless the admission was conditioned on the juvenile's being able to appeal.


OUTCOME: Decision vacated.

 

15 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


B.H. v. Commonwealth


2013-SC-000254-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


494 S.W.3d 467; 2016 Ky. LEXIS 421



March 17, 2016, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 15, 2016.
 [**1] MODIFIED: AUGUST 25, 2016. MODIFIED: APRIL 13, 2016.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2012-CA-001768-DR. WOODFORD CIRCUIT COURT NO. 11-XX-00001; WOODFORD JUVENILE COURT NO. 09-J-00050-004.
B.H. v. Commonwealth, 2016 Ky. LEXIS 106 (Ky., Mar. 17, 2016)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant juvenile's admission was agreed upon between the County Attorney, defendant, and his attorney, and this was a bargained-for result, which gave defendant the opportunity to convince the trial court that he did not need to be committed for sexual-offender treatment, which would involve placement outside his home in a Department of Juvenile Justice facility; [2]-Having entered into his admission unconditionally, and indicating that he did so knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily, with his attorney present and encouraging his plea, defendant waived his right to appeal and thus, the supreme court could not reach the merits of any of defendant's claims raised because there was no proper appeal before the supreme court.


OUTCOME: Vacated and remanded.

 

16 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Jackson v. Commonwealth


2014-SC-000612-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


481 S.W.3d 794; 2016 Ky. LEXIS 10



February 18, 2016, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 10, 2016.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE OLU ALFREDO STEVENS, JUDGE. NO. 13-CR-000616.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant was not entitled to a "no duty to retreat" jury instruction because collecting the money owed for heroin was as much a part of the illegal sale as was the delivery of the heroin under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.1412; [2]-Defendant's juvenile adjudication was properly admitted under Ky. R. Evid. 403 because he did not object to the testimony and made no showing that the testimony differed in any respect from the official record of the juvenile court adjudication, and the jury's decision was not affected by an incorrect impression that a juvenile court "adjudication" was synonymous with a "conviction"; [3]-The trial court could not overturn or disregard the controlling authority that barred the relief defendant sought because only the Kentucky Supreme Court could determine if or when the comity accorded to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.055(2)(a)(6) would no longer apply.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

17 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Blau v. Wolnitzek (In re Winter)


2015-SC-000086-CL


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


482 S.W.3d 768; 2016 Ky. LEXIS 6



February 18, 2016, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 10, 2016.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] THE UNITED STATES DISTRICT COURT. EASTERN DISTRICT OF KENTUCKY, NORTHERN DIVISION COVINGTON, CIVIL NO. 14-119-ART.
Winter v. Wolnitzek, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 17849 (E.D. Ky., Feb. 12, 2015)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Judicial candidates were allowed to affiliate, i.e., portray, themselves as members of a political party without restriction, but could not, under Ky. Sup. Ct. R. 4.300, Canons 5A(1)(b) and 5B(1)(c), portray themselves, either directly or by implication, as the official nominee of a political party; [2]-For purposes of Ky. Sup. Ct. R. 4.300, Canon 5A(1)(b), acting as a leader captured efforts to advance the political agenda of a political party in a less formal way, and thus, one who hosted an event for a political party was acting as a leader for the party; [3]-Ky. Sup. Ct. R. 4.300, Canon 5B(1)(c), extended only to statements made during a campaign which were objectively factually untrue and dido not extend to expressions of subjective opinions or innocuous campaign-trail puffing; [4]-An appointed judge's assertion that she sought to be reelected was materially false.


OUTCOME: Law certified to federal district court.

 

18 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Gray v. Commonwealth


2013-SC-000374-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


480 S.W.3d 253; 2016 Ky. LEXIS 1



February 18, 2016, Rendered


NOTICE: TO BE PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Corrected: April 12, 2016.
Released for Publication April 12, 2016.
Related proceeding at Gray v. Hampton, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 186422 (E.D. Ky., Nov. 9, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM SCOTT CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE PAUL F. ISAACS, JUDGE. NO. 07-CR-00211.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court erred in failing to suppress defendant's confession to officers, as the use of false statements and a phony DNA lab report as the sole basis for hours of unrecorded interrogation offended the Fourteenth Amendment right to due process, and the weight of false evidence against defendant and the pressures exerted by interrogating officers overwhelmed defendant's conscience; [2]-The trial court improperly excluded defendant's alternate perpetrator evidence, as the evidence tended to show that the other individual had motive to commit the crime and the exclusion of evidence prevented defendant from showing that he also had opportunity; [3]-The trial court did not err, under Ky. R. Evid. 702, in refusing to allow a retired police officer to testify to a variety of missteps during the investigation, as he had no published works or professional credentials beyond his years of experience.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

Dillard v. Commonwealth


2013-SC-000425-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


475 S.W.3d 594; 2015 Ky. LEXIS 2008



December 17, 2015, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 7, 2016.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2011-CA-001917-DG. JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT NO. 11-XX-0017.
Dillard v. Commonwealth, 2013 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 435 (Ky. Ct. App., May 31, 2013)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Dismissal of an appeal was appropriate where the district court's order plainly stated that restitution still had to be determined, defendant's conditional plea specifically reserving the issue of restitution did not obviate the need for a final judgment, and thus, the order was not final, appealable order under Ky. R. Civ. P. 54.01.


OUTCOME: Dismissal affirmed.

 

20 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Greater Cincinnati/Northern Ky. Apt. Ass'n v. Campbell County Fiscal Court


2014-SC-000383-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


479 S.W.3d 603; 2015 Ky. LEXIS 1946



October 29, 2015, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 18, 2016.
Rehearing denied by Greater Cincinnati/Northern Ky. Apt. Ass'n v. Campbell Cnty. Fiscal Court, 479 S.W.3d 603, 2016 Ky. LEXIS 53 (Ky., Feb. 18, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM CAMPBELL CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE FRED A. STINE, V, JUDGE. NO. 13-CI-00956.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 65.760(3) was a specific provision that expressly authorized the use of fees to fund 911 emergency telephone services, demonstrated the General Assembly's specific intent to permit local governments to fund 911 telephone services through the imposition of fees, and did not require that the fee be based on use; [2]-Fees authorized by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 65.760 had to bear some reasonable relationship to the benefit received; [3]-The fee imposed by a county to fund its 911 service, which replaced a land line subscriber charge with an annual service fee levied upon each occupied individual residential and commercial unit, was a constitutional and statutorily valid exercise of its authority.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

21 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Brewer v. Commonwealth


2013-SC-000467-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


478 S.W.3d 363; 2015 Ky. LEXIS 1856



September 24, 2015, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 18, 2016.
Rehearing denied by Brewer v. Commonwealth, 478 S.W.3d 363, 2016 Ky. LEXIS 44 (Ky., Feb. 18, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2012-CA-000622-MR. FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT NO. 11-CR-00622.
Brewer v. Commonwealth, 2013 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 483 (Ky. Ct. App., June 14, 2013)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The statute, as well as misdemeanor-sentencing and non-delegation case law, required trifurcation for a conviction under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 508.032; [2]-The first phase of the trifurcated process was the guilt phase where no prior-conviction evidence was admissible, and if the jury found guilt, it fixed punishment; [3]-The second phase was the § 508.032 guilt phase where prior-conviction evidence was admissible, but only prior convictions of fourth-degree assault involving a family member or member of an unmarried couple and if the jury found defendant not guilty in the second phase, judgment was entered imposing the misdemeanor sentence fixed by the jury on the first phase; [4]-The third phase, enhanced sentencing for fourth-degree assault, third or subsequent offense within five years, was conducted in accordance with Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.055.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

Roe v. Commonwealth


2013-SC-000793-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


2015 Ky. LEXIS 2080



September 24, 2015, Rendered


NOTICE:

PLEASE REFER TO THE KENTUCKY RULES REGARDING FINALITY OF OPINIONS. TO BE PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Corrected: November 14, 2016, Modified: May 5, 2016.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JAMES D. ISHMAEL, JR., JUDGE. NO. 12-CR-00037.
Roe v. Commonwealth, 2015 Ky. Unpub. LEXIS 68 (Ky., Sept. 24, 2015)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Lay opinion testimony was not palpable error because it was a Ky. R. Evid. 701 use of witness impressions, a Ky. R. Evid. 803(1) present-sense impression, cured, or outweighed by guilt evidence; [2]-Victim-impact evidence in the guilt phase was not palpable error, under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.055(2)(a)(7), because it said the victim was a loving mother and wife; [3]-Defendant's alternate perpetrator evidence was not wrongly excluded because it had little relevance to this presented defense; [4]-Excluding an African-American juror did not offend Batson because the juror's defense affinity was race-neutral; [5]-Defendant waived a pre-sentence investigation by not cooperating because Ky. R. Crim. P. 11.02(1)'s waiver preempted Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.050(6); [6]-A Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23A.205 cost order was undisturbed despite his indigence because he did not object.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

23 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Sargent v. Shaffer


2013-SC-000111-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


467 S.W.3d 198; 2015 Ky. LEXIS 1745



August 20, 2015, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: CORRECTED: AUGUST 26, 2015.
Released for Publication September 10, 2015.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2011-CA-001696-MR. FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT NO. 10-CI-00680.
Sargent v. Shaffer, 2013 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 92 (Ky. Ct. App., Feb. 1, 2013)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Construed in accordance with its plain terms and obvious meaning, it was readily apparent that, in an applicable civil action where informed consent was an issue, a medical treatment provider had satisfied the duty to obtain the patient's consent only if both Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 304.40-320(1) and (2) were met; [2]-By failing to incorporate the general understanding component of the duty provided in § 304.40-320(2), the trial court's instruction did not accurately set forth the applicable law; [3]-Although the traditional bare bones approach to jury instructions was still valid, the essence of § 304.40-320(2) was one of the structural elements, i.e., the bones, around which the substance of the law of the case was built; [4]-The instruction covering § 304.40-320(1) did not capture all of the requirements of § 304.40-320(2) given the subsections differing functions.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; case remanded to trial court.

Commonwealth v. AT&T Corp.

AT&T Corp. v. Commonwealth, 2013 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 899 (Ky. Ct. App., Nov. 15, 2013)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Court of Appeals erred in determining that a facial constitutional issue raised by a taxpayer was one that the Kentucky Board of Tax Appeals could not decide because the case did not challenge the constitutionality of the administrative process for collecting a tax refund, there were several administrative issues that had to be resolved prior to addressing the constitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 139.505, which necessitated formal written findings in accordance with Ky. Rev. Stat. OUTCOME: Court of Appeals' decision reversed and trial court's order reinstated.

Foley v. Beshear


2013-SC-000777-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


462 S.W.3d 389; 2015 Ky. LEXIS 1636



June 11, 2015, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 2, 2015.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Foley v. Beshear, 136 S. Ct. 797, 193 L. Ed. 2d 723, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 29 (U.S., Jan. 11, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE PHILLIP J. SHEPHERD, JUDGE. NO. 13-CI-00461.
Foley v. Commonwealth, 953 S.W.2d 924, 44:5 Ky. L. Summary 13, 1997 Ky. LEXIS 56 (Ky., Apr. 24, 1997)
Foley v. Commonwealth, 942 S.W.2d 876, 43:12 Ky. L. Summary 11, 1996 Ky. LEXIS 127 (Ky., Apr. 24, 1997)
Baze v. Commonwealth, 965 S.W.2d 817, 44:4 Ky. L. Summary 10, 1997 Ky. LEXIS 40 (Ky., Mar. 27, 1997)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The circuit court properly dismissed two death-row inmates' Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 418.040 complaint for a declaratory judgment because, while they did not address the statute's requirement for an "actual controversy," their strong interest in being considered for clemency created an actual controversy as to whether the state officials' alleged failure to adopt clemency standards and procedures, violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV, the inmates failed to state a claim for relief where Ky. Const. § 77's near complete reliance on the Governor for clemency determinations was not at odds with the minimal procedural safeguards in the Fourteenth Amendment, and the inmates did not advance a reason to suppose that the Governor could not or would not provide procedures as well as decisions to avoid the sort of arbitrariness that might taint a clemency determination.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed.

 

26 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Ballinger v. Commonwealth


2012-SC-000694-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


459 S.W.3d 349; 2015 Ky. LEXIS 1611



May 14, 2015, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 4, 2015.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2011-CA-001248-MR. WARREN CIRCUIT COURT NO. 11-CR-00028.
Commonwealth v. Ballinger, 2012 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1048 (Ky. Ct. App., Sept. 28, 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 189A.010(1), defendant could be prosecuted for a DUI fourth offense, when two prior convictions were not entered when he committed his current crime, because, under the applicable two-pronged approach, they occurred within five years before his current crime, and convictions for the prior crimes were entered before his current conviction, as impaired drivers were subject to both criminal sanctions under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 189A.010(5) and license suspensions under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 189A.070(1), the number of convictions of record at the time of a new conviction determined a suspension's length, and Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 189A.070(1)(e) said "offense" had the same meaning for both purposes; [2]-His guilty plea on one day to separate DUI offenses did not bar treating them as separate convictions because the number of prior crimes controlled.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the Court of Appeals affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Gamble


2013-SC-000141-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


453 S.W.3d 716; 2015 Ky. LEXIS 15



February 19, 2015, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 12, 2015.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2011-CA-001658-MR. JOHNSON CIRCUIT COURT NO. 10-CR-00145.
Gamble v. Commonwealth, 2013 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 91 (Ky. Ct. App., Feb. 1, 2013)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the circuit court was statutorily barred from enhancing defendant's sentence beyond the three-year cap set forth in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.1413(2)(b)(1) by virtue of his persistent felony offender (PFO) conviction. HOLDINGS: [1]-Section 218A.1413(2)(b)(1) did not prohibit defendant's sentence from being enhanced to five years imprisonment by virtue of his status as a PFO; [2]-The General Assembly only excluded first-degree possession of a controlled substance from PFO enhancement eligibility in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.080(8), thereby demonstrating that trafficking in a controlled substance in the second degree was eligible for PFO enhancement.


OUTCOME: Opinion reversed and sentence reinstated.

Parker v. Commonwealth


2011-SC-000662-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


440 S.W.3d 381; 2014 Ky. LEXIS 432



September 18, 2014, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 9, 2014.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2010-CA-001215-MR. JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT NO. 09-CR-001470.
Commonwealth v. Parker, 2011 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 996 (Ky. Ct. App., Sept. 30, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a case involving the suppression of evidence, an appeal filed by the Commonwealth was timely, even though it was inappropriate for Ky. R. Civ. P. 59.05 review, because the Commonwealth forfeited its Rule 59.05 motion before the trial court with an alternative request for findings of fact and conclusions of law under Ky. R. Crim. P. 9.78; [2]-The motion for findings under Rule 9.78 was treated as a Ky. R. Civ. P. 52.02 motion, thus tolling the appeal period under Ky. R. Civ. P. 73.02; [3]-Suppression of evidence found in a vehicle was not warranted because a search was conducted by an officer in an objectively reasonable reliance on clearly established precedent under New York v. Belton and Henry v. Commonwealth; [4]-Therefore, the exclusionary rule did not apply.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the court of appeals affirmed.

Darcy v. Commonwealth


2012-SC-000427-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


441 S.W.3d 77; 2014 Ky. LEXIS 433

McCleery v. Commonwealth, 410 S.W.3d 597, 2013 Ky. LEXIS 407 (Ky., 2013)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a burglary case, the trial court abused its discretion by denying defendant's motion for a continuance without contemplating Ky. Rev. Stat. R. Evid. 404(b) and was properly introduced as evidence.


OUTCOME: The Supreme Court reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

Louisville/Jefferson County Metro Gov't v. O'Shea's-Baxter, LLC


2013-SC-000085-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


438 S.W.3d 379; 2014 Ky. LEXIS 339



August 21, 2014, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 11, 2014.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2011-CA-001583-MR. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT NO. 10-CI-00991.
O'Shea's-Baxter, LLC v. Commonwealth, 2013 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 983 (Ky. Ct. App., Jan. 4, 2013)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 241.075 was void because it violated Ky. Const. §§ 59 and 60; [2]-Section 241.075 imposed a 700-feet restriction between liquor-only licensees on the consolidated local government of Louisville, Kentucky when it could have been made applicable throughout the State by a general act; [3]-The statute did not treat individuals and corporations across the State alike, and it unnecessarily discriminated against potential retail drink licensees in Louisville's consolidated local government; [4]-Therefore, the statute's separate classification of Louisville's consolidated local government for the purpose of limiting the concentration of retail drink licenses was a local and special act in violation of the letter and spirit of §§ 59 and 60.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

St. Clair v. Commonwealth


2011-SC-000774-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


451 S.W.3d 597; 2014 Ky. LEXIS 341



August 21, 2014, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 19, 2015.
Rehearing denied by St. Clair v. Commonwealth, 2015 Ky. LEXIS 53 (Ky., Feb. 11, 2015)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by St. Clair v. Kentucky, 2015 U.S. LEXIS 5215 (U.S., Oct. 5, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM BULLITT CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE GEOFFREY P. MORRIS, JUDGE. NO. 92-CR-000.10-002.
St. Clair v. Commonwealth, 2010 Ky. LEXIS 249 (Ky., Sept. 23, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Pursuant to the supreme court's review under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.075, defendant's death sentence was proper because the death sentence was not imposed under the influence of prejudice, passion, or any other arbitrary factor as the evidence channeled the jury to consider the circumstances of defendant's crimes, including the effect of the crimes on the victim's daughter, and defendant's personal characteristics, such as his cold and calculating approach to murder; the evidence supported the jury's conclusion that the murder was committed by a person with a prior record of conviction for a capital offense under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.025(2)(a)1; and, although defendant was not convicted of multiple murders in the current case, he had committed multiple murders, and that fact appropriately bore on whether his death sentence was proportionate.


OUTCOME: Conviction and sentence affirmed.

 

34 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Tibbs v. Bunnell


2012-SC-000603-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


448 S.W.3d 796; 2014 Ky. LEXIS 333



August 21, 2014, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 18, 2014.
Rehearing denied by Tibbs v. Bunnell, 2014 Ky. LEXIS 599 (Ky., Dec. 18, 2014)
Later proceeding at Tibbs v. Bunnell, 136 S. Ct. 290, 193 L. Ed. 2d 18, 2015 U.S. LEXIS 5509 (U.S., 2015)
Motion granted by, Petition denied by Tibbs v. Bunnell, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 4177 (U.S., June 27, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2012-CA-000916-OA. FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT NO. 12-CI-00392.
Tibbs v. Bunnell, 2012 Ky. App. LEXIS 307 (Ky. Ct. App., Aug. 16, 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the court of appeals erred in limiting the privilege to documents employing a "self-examining analysis" rather than the language used in the Patient Safety and Quality Improvement Act of 2005, 42 U.S.C.S. § 299b-21 et seq. HOLDINGS: [1]-While incident information could be relevant to its endeavors under the Act, it was not, nor could it be, patient safety work product since its collection, creation, maintenance, and utilization was mandated by the Commonwealth of Kentucky as part of its regulatory oversight of its healthcare facilities; [2]-Congress never intended the Act to deprive the states of state-mandated information relevant to their regulatory duties, 42 U.S.C.S. § 299b-21(7)(B); [3]-Thus, information normally contained in an incident report was not privileged under the Act and could be discovered, following an in camera review, and its information compelled.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

Bullitt Fiscal Court v. Bullitt County Bd. of Health


2013-SC-000023-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


434 S.W.3d 29; 2014 Ky. LEXIS 237



June 19, 2014, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 10, 2014.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2011-CA-001798-MR. BULLITT CIRCUIT COURT NO. 11-CI-00348.
Bullitt County Bd. of Health v. Bullitt County Fiscal Court, 2012 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1067 (Ky. Ct. App., Dec. 7, 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether appellee county health board's (board) smoking ban was valid. HOLDINGS: [1]-The ban was invalid because it exceeded the board's authority in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 212.230(1)(c), since the statute could not be construed as a paramount rule from which the ban was derived, as this construction would delegate the Commonwealth's police power too broadly, contrary to Ky. Const. §§ 27 and 28, and the statute was a limited delegation of legislative authority evidenced by the qualification that health boards could adopt, except as otherwise provided by law, administrative regulations not in conflict with the administrative regulations of the Cabinet for Health and Family Services; [2]-The ban was also invalid because the legislature which adopted the statute did not intend or foresee that it would be invoked by an administrative agency to prohibit smoking in public places.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

Curd v. Ky. State Bd. of Licensure for Prof'l Eng'rs & Land Surveyors


2012-SC-000165-DG, 2012-SC-000169-DG

June 19, 2014, Rendered

CASE SUMMARY:

OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part.

Kirby v. Lexington Theol. Seminary


2012-SC-000519-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


426 S.W.3d 597; 2014 Ky. LEXIS 161; 122 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1836; 38 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 212; 97 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P45,059



April 17, 2014, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 8, 2014.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2010-CA-001798-MR. FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT NO. 09-CI-04480.
Kant v. Lexington Theol. Seminary, 426 S.W.3d 587, 2014 Ky. LEXIS 160 (Ky., Apr. 17, 2014)
Kirby v. Lexington Theol. Seminary, 2012 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1007 (Ky. Ct. App., July 27, 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Kentucky adopted the ministerial exception because the U.S. Constitution mandated it; [2]-The exception was an affirmative defense, not a jurisdiction limit, because the issue was entitlement to relief, not power to hear a case; [3]-The exception applied because appellee employer was a religious institution, and the employee was a ministerial employee, given his involvement in the employer's mission and his teaching; [4]-His Ky. Rev. Stat. OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

City of Lebanon v. Goodin


2011-SC-000468-DG

City of Lebanon v. Goodin, 2011 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 968 (Ky. Ct. App., July 15, 2011)

OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The lower court erred in granting the landowners summary judgment on an action to invalidate an annexation where it erroneously applied a natural or regular standard to the city's decision, the terms adjacent and contiguous in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 81A.410(1)(b) were not to be read to be equivalent, and the city had fully complied with the statutory requirements in that the northern boundary of the territory touched the city's current municipal border and the territory was suitable for urban development; [2]-The city did not violate Ky. Const. § 2 where the decision to annex nearby territory was rationally connected to the city's power to promote community values and effect policies in the best interests of the community.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; case remanded for entry of summary judgment in the city's favor.

Commonwealth v. Wright


2012-SC-000368-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


415 S.W.3d 606; 2013 Ky. LEXIS 652

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1]

Commonwealth v. Wright, 2012 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1006 (Ky. Ct. App., May 25, 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The circuit court properly denied the Commonwealth's motion to revoke defendant's probation based upon his failure to pay restitution because the circuit court lacked jurisdiction to revoke defendant's probation as his fixed probationary period had expired, and Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.033(8) automatically extend probation.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

51 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Dunlap v. Commonwealth


2010-SC-000226-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


435 S.W.3d 537; 2013 Ky. LEXIS 292



June 20, 2013, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 20, 2014.
Rehearing denied by Dunlap v. Commonwealth, 2014 Ky. LEXIS 73 (Ky., Feb. 20, 2014)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Dunlap v. Ky., 2014 U.S. LEXIS 6466 (U.S., Oct. 6, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM LIVINGSTON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE CLEARANCE A. WOODALL, III, JUDGE. NO. 09-CR-00027.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the Livingston Circuit Court (Kentucky) to three counts each of capital murder, capital kidnapping, and tampering with physical evidence, and one count each of attempted murder, first-degree kidnapping, first-degree rape, first-degree arson, and first-degree burglary. Defendant was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by failing to suppress his statements under U.S. Const. amend. V because his Miranda rights were violated. The supreme court disagreed. Although a detective's question to defendant, "do you know why we are here" constituted a custodial interrogation, an incriminating response was not coerced. The detective arrived at defendant's home with several law enforcement officers and the S.W.A.T. team; under those circumstances, he should have reasonably expected an incriminating response. Defendant was advised of his Miranda rights at the sheriff's office and checked each of them on a written form. Defendant stated he understood them, he voluntarily waived them, and said he would make a statement without counsel present. Neither officer saw any indication that defendant was intoxicated or otherwise unable to speak on an intelligent and voluntary basis. Therefore, defendant's waiver of his Miranda rights at the sheriff's office was made knowingly, rationally, and intelligently.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Murray v. Commonwealth


2011-SC-000081-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


399 S.W.3d 398; 2013 Ky. LEXIS 230



May 23, 2013, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 25, 2013.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE SUSAN LYNN SCHULTZ, JUDGE. NO. 09-CR-000 199-002.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) found appellant guilty of two counts of complicity to commit murder, one count of first-degree robbery, one count of first-degree burglary, and two counts of tampering with physical evidence. Appellant challenged the judgment of conviction and sentence as a matter of right under Ky. Const. § 110(2)(b).


OVERVIEW: Testimony at trial and evidence presented during discovery shows that appellant and co-defendant took items, including five knives, from the army surplus store where the first victim worked and was murdered. Both appellant and co-defendant carried a knife stolen from the army surplus store with them to the second victim's apartment. Finally, there was evidence to show the knife used to stab the second victim was from the army surplus store. Thus, joinder of the murder counts was appropriate under Ky. R. Crim. P. 6.18. In addition, appellant was not merely a facilitator of the first murder as he was at the scene of the crime, stole various items from the store where the victim worked, helped co-defendant carry the loot back to the homeless shelter, stored the bags of stolen goods in a storage unit rented under his name, and both he and co-defendant made repeated trips to the unit to retrieve items. Thus, the trial judge was correct in refusing to instruct on criminal facilitation under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 506.080 and instructing the jury on complicity under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 520.020.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment of conviction and sentence.

Grider v. Commonwealth


2012-SC-000454-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


404 S.W.3d 859; 2013 Ky. LEXIS 229



May 23, 2013, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 29, 2013.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE SUSAN SCHULTZ GIBSON, JUDGE. NOS. 08-CR-003131 AND 11-CR-003681.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was tried as a youthful offender, appealed his conviction for murder, first-degree robbery, and intimidating a participant in the legal process and the life sentence imposed by the Jefferson Circuit Court, Kentucky.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in failing to strike a juror. Absent any evidence of actual bias, the sole fact that the juror was an assistant county attorney was not sufficient ground to sustain a motion to strike for cause. At the time of the trial, the juror practiced exclusively in civil cases and was unacquainted with the Commonwealth's prosecuting attorneys. His argument was not preserved for review that Ky. R, Crim. P. 9.40 exceeded the authority granted to the Supreme Court of Kentucky in Ky. Const. § 116 and that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 29A.290(2)(b) was unconstitutional. He had not complied with the notification requirements of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 418.075(1), which were mandatory. He did not argue that a sentence life without the possibility of parole for 25 years was an unconstitutional sentence as applied to juveniles. He unsuccessfully argued that since he could not be sentenced to death, there was no procedure by which to find, present, and instruct the jury on aggravating factors. Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.025 did not prevent the jury from hearing evidence of aggravating circumstances.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Newcomb v. Commonwealth

56 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Ky. S. Coal Corp. v. Ky. Energy & Env't Cabinet Formerly the Envtl. & Pub. Prot. Cabinet


2010-SC-000029-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


396 S.W.3d 804; 2013 Ky. LEXIS 86



April 25, 2013, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 16, 2013.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2008-CA-002229-MR. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT NO. 06-CI-00081.
Ky. S. Coal Corp. v. Ky. Energy, 2009 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1035 (Ky. Ct. App., Dec. 11, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant coal company sought review in the Court of Appeals (Kentucky) of a trial court's judgment affirming the decision of appellee Kentucky Energy and Environment Cabinet (Cabinet) denying the company's application to renew a surface and underground coal mining permit due to a bona fide dispute over its right of entry to land within its permit's boundaries. The Court of Appeals affirmed the trial court, and the company sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found the expiration of a surface lease previously adjudicated by another court created a bona fide dispute over the company's rights to mine coal on the tract. The supreme court held the Cabinet properly denied the renewal application because a bona fide dispute existed over the company's right of entry. The prior judgment created a bona fide dispute because (1) it declared the company's predecessor owned coal and mining rights in and underlying the tract and (2) stated the terms of a 15-year surface lease, which had expired, that could be interpreted to affect the predecessor's right of entry to underground mining, and (3) that judgment bound the company. The Cabinet could not renew the permit because it had no authority to adjudicate the property dispute within the jurisdiction of the court issuing the prior judgment. The Cabinet did not adjudicate the company's property rights because the Cabinet only properly found uncertainty as to the company's right of entry. It was irrelevant that the tract's new surface owner did not intervene because (1) nothing required intervention, and (2) nothing showed the owner's waiver, lease or deed in favor of the company.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Court of Appeals was affirmed.

Hale v. Commonwealth


2011-SC-000115-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


396 S.W.3d 841; 2013 Ky. LEXIS 90



April 25, 2013, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 16, 2013.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2009-CA-002273-MR. CHRISTIAN CIRCUIT COURT NO.09-CR-00064.
Hale v. Commonwealth, 2011 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 62 (Ky. Ct. App., Jan. 21, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree unlawful transaction with a minor, under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 530.064(1) (2007). Despite his argument that the statute did not apply unless the perpetrator induced a minor to commit a crime, the Court of Appeals (Kentucky) affirmed the conviction, and defendant sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant said he was entitled to a directed verdict because the minor victim was induced to submit to a crime but not to commit one. The supreme court held Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 530.064 (2007) did not require that the minor be induced to commit a crime because the "illegal sexual activity" proscribed by the statute was not limited to sexual activity committed by a minor victim that was illegal for the minor to commit and for which the minor could be sanctioned, as any overlap between the statute and other statutes prohibiting sexual abuse of a minor spoke to the wide diversity of sexual conduct the statutes were meant to regulate, leaving to prosecutorial and grand jury discretion the fitting of any charge to the conduct alleged. Prosecutorial misconduct did not taint defendant's conviction because any such misconduct (1) was not objected to, and (2) was not flagrant or palpable, as the prosecutor's characterization of defendant's minimization of the crime and attempt to shift responsibility to the victim as "offensive" and references to the victim's youth and lost virginity properly responded to defendant's claim of prosecutorial overreaching.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

 

58 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Stinson v. Commonwealth


2011-SC-000615-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


396 S.W.3d 900; 2013 Ky. LEXIS 87



April 25, 2013, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 16, 2013.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2010-CA-001647-MR, MADISON CIRCUIT COURT NO. 09-CR-00316.
Stinson v. Commonwealth, 2011 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 946 (Ky. Ct. App., Sept. 9, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered an Alford guilty plea to first-degree sexual abuse, in violation of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 510.110(1)(d). The Court of Appeals, Kentucky, affirmed, and defendant sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The Supreme Court of Kentucky held that lack of consent is an element under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 510.110(1)(d), and a person under 18 years old cannot consent to sexual contact from a person who is in a position of special trust or authority. Such behavior is sexual abuse in the first degree, and does not require an additional showing of lack of consent. In the current case, the lack-of-consent element was satisfied by the fact that the victim was unable to consent, as she was 17 at the time of the offense and was subjected to sexual contact by a person in a position of authority or special trust within the meaning of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.045(1)(b). Defendant was the victim's uncle and the head of her household at the time of the offense. Defendant lacked standing to raise vagueness and overbreadth challenges. The court nevertheless held that the requirement that the perpetrator be in a "position of authority" and/or "position of special trust" does not render the statute void for vagueness, and that deterring sexual conduct between persons who are 16 to 18 years of age does not rendered it unconstitutionally overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the Court of Appeals.

 

59 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Flick v. Estate of Christina Wittich


2010-SC-000664-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


396 S.W.3d 816; 2013 Ky. LEXIS 89



April 25, 2013, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 16, 2013.
On remand at, Remanded by Flick v. Estate of Wittich, 2015 Ky. App. LEXIS 12 (Ky. Ct. App., Feb. 6, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2009-CA-002378-MR, FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT NO. 08-CI-04294.
Flick v. Estate of Wittich, 2012 Ky. LEXIS 272 (Ky., Feb. 15, 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee estate successfully sued appellant alleged tortfeasor for wrongful death. The Court of Appeals (Kentucky) dismissed the tortfeasor's appeal for failing to name the estate's co-administrators in his notice of appeal. The tortfeasor was granted discretionary review.


OVERVIEW: The caption in the tortfeasor's notice of appeal named the decedent's estate, "et al." as "plaintiffs," and himself as "defendant," the notice identified the judgment appealed but did not designate an appellant or appellee, and it was served on the co-administrators' counsel. The supreme court held it was error to dismiss the appeal because omitting the co-administrators was not fatal, as (1) any judicial result bound them, since only they could defend the estate's claims, under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 395.195(19), so they were inexorably linked with it in litigation, and (2) the notice did not bar complete appellate relief, as only they, having notice, could litigate the appeal. It was also error to dismiss the appeal because (1) the co-administrators had notice, constituting substantial compliance with Ky. R. Civ. P. 73.03, and (2) they showed no prejudice, as the notice did not cause them to breach their fiduciary duties, since, having notice, they breached those duties only by ignoring the notice, which did not reflect on its sufficiency. The tortfeasor preserved the sufficiency of his notice because deciding the issue was central to the supreme court's review.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Court of Appeals was reversed, and the case was remanded to that Court.

Commonwealth v. Ky. Ret. Sys.


2010-SC-000809-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


396 S.W.3d 833; 2013 Ky. LEXIS 84



April 25, 2013, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 16, 2013.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2009-CA-000728-MR. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT NO. 09-CI-00087.
Bd. of Trs. of Ky. Ret. Sys. v. Commonwealth, 251 S.W.3d 334, 2008 Ky. App. LEXIS 102 (Ky. Ct. App., 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Kentucky Court of Appeals affirmed the trial court's judgment that denied defendant Commonwealth's motion to dismiss the lawsuit filed against it by plaintiff retirement system members seeking a declaration that a statute allowing for a suspension of retirement payments upon reemployment with a public employer was unconstitutional, due to the Commonwealth's sovereign immunity. The state supreme court granted discretionary review.


OVERVIEW: The retirement system members sued the Commonwealth under the Declaratory Judgment Act and sought a determination that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 61.637(1), allowing for the suspension of the retirement benefits of a retiree upon reemployment by a public employer, was unconstitutional. The trial court denied the Commonwealth's motion to dismiss based upon its claim of sovereign immunity. The appellate court affirmed. The state supreme court first found that the legislature waived the Commonwealth's right to sovereign immunity in actions brought against the Commonwealth under the Declaratory Judgment Act and had the authority to do so under Ky. Const. § 231. It then found that even if it had not done so, the doctrine of sovereign immunity was not applicable to declaratory judgment actions because to allow a contrary result would permit the Commonwealth to act knowing that the legality of its conduct could never be challenged. It also found that the Commonwealth was a necessary party that could be represented by the relevant Commonwealth agency and that the state attorney general could opt out of the suit because the Commonwealth already was adequately represented.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the judgments of the appellate court and the trial court.

 

61 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Allen v. Commonwealth


2010-SC-000353-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


395 S.W.3d 451; 2013 Ky. LEXIS 30



March 21, 2013, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 30, 2013.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2009-CA-000504-MR. JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT NO. 08-CR-001927.
Allen v. Commonwealth, 2010 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 409 (Ky. Ct. App., May 14, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of perjury for lying in a criminal complaint and of theft by deception for obtaining the discharge of a vehicle loan (which she had allegedly co-signed for her boyfriend) by lying to the finance company and saying her name had been forged on the loan documents. The Court of Appeals, Kentucky, affirmed, and defendant sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The Supreme Court of Kentucky held that the evidence was sufficient to avoid a directed verdict on the conviction for theft by deception. The Commonwealth sufficiently proved that defendant obtained property because she obtained the lender's contractual right to collect on the debt. The fact that defendant did not receive tangible property, like the truck itself or money, did not mean she did not commit theft by deception. The finance company's partial reliance on its own internal investigation did not negate the element of reliance because defendant's identity-theft affidavit was also part of the reason for the discharge. The court reversed the convictions, however, because defendant was entitled to ask on cross-examination about the conduct underlying the boyfriend's prior misdemeanor convictions for giving a false name to a peace officer. Ky. R. Evid. 608 and 609 allowed some inquiry as to the conduct underlying a criminal conviction, so long as the conduct was probative of truthfulness or untruthfulness. The error was not harmless because the evidence went to the core of the defense and would have impeached the character and credibility of the Commonwealth's star witness.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the convictions.

 

62 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Ousley


2011-SC-000403-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


393 S.W.3d 15; 2013 Ky. LEXIS 43



March 21, 2013, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 11, 2013.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2010-CA-001579-MR. FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT NO. 10-CR-000287.
Ousley v. Commonwealth, 2011 Ky. App. LEXIS 110 (Ky. Ct. App., June 24, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to first-degree trafficking in a controlled substance (methamphetamine), trafficking in marijuana within 1,000 yards of a school, and possession of drug paraphernalia. The Kentucky Court of Appeals reversed defendant's convictions. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trash pulls were illegal under U.S. Const. amend. IV. The supreme court agreed. Defendant used the area where the trash cans were located for home storage, staging yard work, and parking his car. The activities defendant used the area for were quintessential "activities of domestic life." There was no public right of access through curtilage that did not involve interaction with, or the benefit or convenience of, the homeowner. Instead, police must attempt to contact the resident of the home upon entering the curtilage to avoid violating the Fourth Amendment. The officer never tried to contact defendant or other residents of the house; indeed, the officer's chosen approach to investigating--a covert trash pull--depended entirely on not encountering the residents. The officer never intended to go to the front door and engage in such business with defendant. Instead, he went directly to the trash cans under cover of darkness to search them. His goal was not engaging the homeowner, but to approach the house under cover and to avoid detection, thereby avoiding interacting with defendant at all.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Simmons


2011-SC-000118-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


394 S.W.3d 903; 2013 Ky. LEXIS 32



March 21, 2013, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 11, 2013.
Decision reached on appeal by Simmons v. Commonwealth, 2015 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 95 (Ky. Ct. App., Feb. 6, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NOS. 2008-CA-001340-MR AND 2008-CA-001374-MR. MADISON CIRCUIT COURT NO. 08-CR-00004-002.
Smith v. Commonwealth, 2011 Ky. App. LEXIS 9 (Ky. Ct. App., Jan. 21, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree trafficking in a controlled substance and sentenced to 15 years in prison. The Court of Appeals of Kentucky remanded the case to the trial court for a hearing on whether defendant had waived the right to a twelve-person jury. The Commonwealth sought review.


OVERVIEW: The court held that under Ky. Const. § 7 a twelve-person jury was a fundamental right in Kentucky, and that any waiver of that right had to be knowingly and voluntarily made by the defendant personally, not by his counsel unilaterally as a trial-management decision. The court held that the trial court erred by not insuring on the record that defendant had been apprised of his right to a twelve-person jury and personally agreed to waive it because defense counsel stipulated to proceeding with less than twelve jurors and defendant only seemingly acquiesced. A remand was necessary for the trial court to conduct an evidentiary hearing to determine if defendant knowingly and voluntarily consented to that decision. If, after an evidentiary hearing, the trial court found that defendant validly waived his right to a twelve-person jury, his conviction was to be reinstated. Otherwise, his conviction was to be reversed with defendant subject to retrial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the case was remanded to the trial court for additional proceedings.

Stacy v. Commonwealth

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM BOYLE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE DARREN PECKLER, JUDGE. NO. 10-CR-00037.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions in the Boyle Circuit Court, Kentucky, of first-degree riot and being a first-degree persistent felony offender.


OVERVIEW: Appellate court held that there was no conflict of interest adversely affecting defendant's lawyer's performance; defendant's bare assertion that a conflict existed because his lawyers represented other defendants in alleged violation of Ky. Ordway v. Commonwealth


2010-SC-000783-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


391 S.W.3d 762; 2013 Ky. LEXIS 3



February 21, 2013, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 14, 2013.
Decision reached on appeal by Ordway v. Commonwealth, 2016 Ky. Unpub. LEXIS 66 (Ky., Sept. 22, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE PAMELA GOODWINE, JUDGE. NO. 07-CR-01319.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Fayette Circuit Court, (Kentucky) of two counts of intentional murder and was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by permitting an officer to testify, from his experience investigating self-defense related homicides, how persons who legitimately exercised the right of self-protection typically behaved. The supreme court agreed. The officer opined that defendant did not act like those who had lawfully protected themselves but, had instead acted like those who were fabricating a self-protection defense. The testimony was incompetent under Ky. R. Evid. 406 because it permitted the police detective to authoritatively suggest how innocent persons behaved after they lawfully engaged in an act of self-defense, and to then, with some measure of certainty, exclude defendant from that class of persons based upon his conduct following the shooting. The opinion of an experienced and respected officer that defendant's conduct did not match the stereo-typical conduct of an innocent person acting in self-defense authoritatively portrayed defendant's defense as a fabrication. That testimony was clearly devastating to defendant's claim of self-defense, and accordingly, reversal was required.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

 

66 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Osborne v. Keeney


2010-SC-000397-DG, 2010-SC-000430-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


399 S.W.3d 1; 2012 Ky. LEXIS 203



December 20, 2012, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 20, 2013.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NOS. 2007-CA-002112-MR AND 2007-CA-002177-MR. JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT NO. 06-CI-001717. ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NOS. 2007-CA-002112-MR AND 2007-CA-002177-MR. JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT NO. 06-CI-001717.
Keeney v. Osborne, 2010 Ky. App. LEXIS 57 (Ky. Ct. App., Mar. 5, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant client and appellee attorney petitioned for discretionary review after the Court of Appeals (Kentucky) affirmed, in part, a judgment in favor of the client in the client's legal malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: The client sued her attorney, claiming he breached his professional duty to her by failing to file suit against the pilot before the statute of limitations expired. Because of the breach, the client alleged that she lost the ability to recover from the pilot for losses she suffered as a result of his crashing his airplane into her home. The jury decided the case in the client's favor, and the appellate court vacated a large portion of the damage award. The supreme court granted the parties' petitions for discretionary review and reversed, stating that the trial court erred when it failed to instruct the jury on the pilot's negligence. The proper method for trying legal malpractice claims was the suit-within-a-suit, which required the trial court to instruct the jury as if it were trying the underlying tort case before instructing the same jury on the legal malpractice claim. Further, the supreme court aligned with those jurisdictions that prohibited recovery of lost punitive damages in legal malpractice actions.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment was reversed and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the supreme court's opinion.

W.B. v. Commonwealth

68 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Wright v. Commonwealth


2011-SC-000191-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


2012 Ky. LEXIS 170



October 25, 2012, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified by Wright v. Commonwealth, 2012 Ky. LEXIS 496 (Ky., Oct. 25, 2012)
Modified and rehearing denied by Wright v. Commonwealth, 2013 Ky. LEXIS 209 (Ky., Feb. 21, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
ON APPEAL FROM CAMPBELL CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE FRED A. STINE, V., JUDGE. NO. 10-CR-00177.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Campbell Circuit Court (Kentucky) of first-degree fleeing or evading police, fourth-degree assault, possession of marijuana, and being a first-degree persistent felony offender (PFO). Defendant received a sentence of twenty years' imprisonment and was fined $600. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court issued erroneous jury instructions on the fleeing or evading police charge. The supreme court agreed. No mention was made of the statutory term, "unmarried couple" in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 403.720. The instructions were at odds with Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 520.095, which required the jury to find beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was "fleeing immediately after committing an act of domestic violence as defined in § 403.720." Absent a finding that the participants in an alleged domestic altercation were an unmarried couple, mere roommates could be charged with having domestically abused one another. The jury was not instructed to find that defendant and the complainant were members of an unmarried couple. Thus, the tendered instructions erroneously failed to require the correct findings. Because the jury was not properly instructed as to the domestic violence element (in that the trial court failed to include a definition of an "unmarried couple") the trial court's error was prejudicial.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences for first-degree fleeing or evading and first-degree PFO were reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings. The portions of defendant's sentences for fourth-degree assault and possession of marijuana imposing fines were vacated. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


382 S.W.3d 835; 2012 Ky. LEXIS 175



October 25, 2012, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 15, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NOS. 2008-CA-001493-DG AND 2009-CA-001046-DG. GRAVES CIRCUIT COURT NOS. 08-XX-00003, 08-XX-00004 AND 08-XX-00005. GRAVES DISTRICT COURT NOS. 07-T-02681, 07-T-02873 AND 07-T-03789. ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NOS. 2008-CA-001493-DG AND 2009-CA-001046-DG. GRAVES CIRCUIT COURT NOS. 09-XX-00002, 09-XX-00003, 09-XX-00004, 09-XX-00005, 09-XX-00006, 09-XX-00007,09-XX-00008, 09-XX-00009, 09-XX-00010 AND 09-XX-00011. GRAVES DISTRICT COURT NOS. 08-T-00609, 08-T-00637, 08-T-00737, 08-T-01006, 08-T-01074, 08-T-0 1134, 08-T-01224,08-T-01309, 08-T-01383, 08-T-01459, 08-T-01525, 08-T-01526, 08-T-01532, 08-T-01713 AND 08-T-01774.
Gingerich v. Commonwealth, 2011 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 963 (Ky. Ct. App., June 3, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant drivers sought review of an opinion from the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which affirmed their convictions and fines for violating Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 189.820 by not displaying a slow-moving vehicle emblem on their horse-and-buggy vehicles.


OVERVIEW: The drivers asserted that the brightly colored emblem conflicted with their religious beliefs, which required plainness, and that they should be allowed to use gray reflective tape instead. The court stated that the free-exercise-of-religion protections in Ky. Const. §§ 1, 5 provided no more protection than the First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I. Accordingly, federal case law was relevant to determining the appropriate standard of review under Kentucky law. The court held that governmental enactments that provided for the public health, safety, and welfare, and that were statutes of general applicability only incidentally affecting the practice of religion, were subject to rational basis review under Kentucky law. Enactments that directly prohibited or restrained a religious practice were subject to a strict scrutiny standard of review. Because § 189.820 applied to all slow-moving vehicles on the public highways, did not prohibit any religious practice, and was aimed at public general safety, the rational basis standard of review applied. There was ample rational basis for a statute regulating slow-moving vehicles for safety reasons; thus, § 189.820 was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the opinion of the court of appeals.
