Derry v. Commonwealth


2006-SC-000181-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


274 S.W.3d 439; 2008 Ky. LEXIS 316



December 18, 2008, Rendered


NOTICE: TO BE PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 8, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2004-CA-000959. METCALFE CIRCUIT COURT NO. 03-CR-00019.
Derry v. Commonwealth, 2005 Ky. App. LEXIS 287 (Ky. Ct. App., Oct. 7, 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Kentucky Court of Appeals entered a judgment that affirmed defendant's conviction on one count of Sexual Abuse in the First Degree. The state supreme court granted discretionary review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with rape, sodomy, and sexual abuse in an indictment filed in the first county. The case went to trial there. The jury was empanelled and sworn, and some testimony was taken. At some point, the Commonwealth was notified that the crime actually occurred in the second county. The trial court in the first county granted defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment. The Commonwealth then indicted defendant in the second county. The trial court in the second county overruled defendant's double jeopardy objection. Defendant later entered a conditional plea to the sexual abuse charge, and was sentenced. The appellate court held that double jeopardy did not bar defendant's second county prosecution and affirmed his conviction. The state supreme court found that he was not entitled to dismissal of the second county indictment because jeopardy had not attached during his first trial county; trial there was simply in the wrong venue, which was not jurisdictional, and no double jeopardy prohibition attached under either Ky. Const. § 13 or U.S. Const. amend. V because the mistrial in the first county resulted from defendant's own motion and his guilt was not decided.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the appellate court's judgment.

 

151 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Hall v. Hospitality Res., Inc.


2007-SC-000153-WC


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


276 S.W.3d 775; 2008 Ky. LEXIS 288



November 26, 2008, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Hall v. Hospitality Res., Inc., 2009 Ky. LEXIS 131 (Ky., Mar. 19, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 2005-CA-001887-WC. WORKERS' COMPENSATION BOARD NO. 95-WC-35309.
Hall v. Hospitality Res., Inc., 2007 Ky. App. LEXIS 8 (Ky. Ct. App., Jan. 12, 2007)



DISPOSITION: REVERSING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant workers' compensation claimant filed a motion to reopen her claim for workers' compensation benefits. The claimant appealed a Kentucky Court of Appeals' opinion affirming a decision of the Kentucky Workers' Compensation Board denying the motion as untimely because Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.125(3)'s four-year statute of limitation for motions to reopen was to be calculated only from the date of the original award.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court noted that the claimant was receiving temporary total disability benefits and had not reached maximum medical improvement (MMI) when the limitation period allegedly ran. She could not have avoided the limitation period by pre-filing and then abating the motion to reopen until she reached MMI. Putting together the 803 Ky. Admin. Regs. 25:010, § 4(6)(a) documentation could only begin after MMI was attained. The evidentiary standards for reopening were controlled by § 342.125(3) on the date of injury, but the limitation period was governed by a 1996 amendment. The reference in § 342.125(3) to the "the original award or order granting or denying benefits" referred to the original award and any subsequent order granting or denying benefits. The claimant's motion to reopen was timely. Cruse v. Aristech Chemical Co., No. 2004-SC-0291-WC, 2005 WL 119771, (January 20, 2005), Cook v. Unicorn Min., No. 2003-SC-0616-WC, 2004 WL 1908114, (August 26, 2004), and Wray v. Allied Systems, No. 2004-SC-002122-WC, 2005 WL 1058862, (Ky. App. 2005), were reversed. Finally, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 342.320 and 342.310, and Ky. R. Civ. P. 11 deterred the filing of frivolous motions.


OUTCOME: The decision of the appellate court was reversed. The matter was remanded to the Board for such further proceedings as were necessary and appropriate.

Commonwealth v. Carneal


2006-SC-000653-DG, 2007-SC-000203-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


274 S.W.3d 420; 2008 Ky. LEXIS 294



November 26, 2008, Rendered


NOTICE: TO BE PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 19, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Commonwealth v. Carneal, 2009 Ky. LEXIS 720 (Ky., Feb. 19, 2009)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Carneal v. Kentucky, 558 U.S. 906, 130 S. Ct. 274, 175 L. Ed. 2d 184, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 5932 (2009)
Related proceeding at Carneal v. Donahue, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 2027 (W.D. Ky., Jan. 12, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2004-CA-001534-MR. McCRACKEN CIRCUIT COURT NO. 97-CR-00350.
Carneal v. Commonwealth, 2006 Ky. App. LEXIS 157 (Ky. Ct. App., May 26, 2006)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING IN PART AND REVERSING IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Appeals (Kentucky) reversing the circuit court's denial of petitioner inmate's motion for post-conviction relief seeking withdrawal of his guilty plea. The appellate court found that the Ky. R. Crim. P. 10.06 and Ky. R. Civ. P. 60.02(f) claims were untimely and that the statute of limitations had not begun to run on the Ky. R. Crim. P. 11.42 claim. The Commonwealth appealed and the inmate cross appealed the issue of timeliness.


OVERVIEW: The court had not addressed, in a published opinion, whether the Ky. R. Crim. P. 11.42 limitation statute applied to the inmate's claims of mental incompetence and ineffective assistance of counsel, but it held that, for purposes of post-conviction relief, a youthful offender's original sentencing order was a final judgment and that the inmate's motion was untimely--it was filed more than three years after sentencing. Reports filed at the 18-year-old hearing indicated that his mental condition stabilized during juvenile detention, that he meaningfully participated in group therapy, and that he earned a high school diploma. In adult corrections, he was treated with more effective medication and earned credits towards an associate's degree. In light of his intermittent competence, his condition did not prevent compliance with the Rule 11.42 such that equitable tolling was appropriate. To interpret information previously suppressed as unknown facts under Rule 11.42(10)(a) would set an explosive precedent. Rule 11.42 was constitutional because it did not restrict access to habeas relief pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. § 419.020 or Ky. Const. § 16; rather, it existed simultaneously.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the holding that the statute of limitations was tolled until the inmate attained the age of eighteen and reversed the opinion of the appellate court as to the inmate's motion. The court affirmed affirm appellate court as to the Ky. R. Civ. P. 60.02 and Ky. R. Crim. P. 10.02 motions, and reinstated the circuit court's judgment.

Workforce Dev. Cabinet v. Gaines


2005-SC-000965-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


276 S.W.3d 789; 2008 Ky. LEXIS 300; 28 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 888



November 26, 2008, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Workforce Dev. Cabinet v. Gaines, 2009 Ky. LEXIS 137 (Ky., Mar. 19, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NO. 2004-CA-001146-MR. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT NO. 02-CI-01523.
Gaines v. Workforce Dev. Cabinet, 2005 Ky. App. LEXIS 241 (Ky. Ct. App., Nov. 10, 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee public employee brought, inter alia, a whistleblower claim under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 61.102 against appellant state agency in the circuit court. The circuit court granted summary judgment to the state agency on the whistleblower claim. The Court of Appeals of Kentucky reversed the grant of summary judgment as to the whistleblower claim. The state agency appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee claimed that she was transferred to a less desirable office as retaliation for reporting a document purge by employees of the state agency. When the employee's attorney contacted an attorney for the state agency, another state agency conducted an investigation of the matter, but concluded that there was no wrongdoing. The intermediate appellate court concluded that the state agency was not entitled to a judgment as a matter of law, because an internal report to the state agency qualified as a report to any other appropriate body or authority under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 61.102. The state supreme court found that the evidence presented a genuine issue of material fact as to whether there was a causal connection between the employee's report and her transfer. The case also presented a genuine issue of material fact as to the ultimate issue: whether the employee was retaliated against as a result of her report. These were questions for a jury. Additionally, the employee made her report to her own division of the agency, which certainly had the power to remedy the situation. Therefore, it could not be said that the state agency was entitled to a judgment as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed. The partial summary judgment in favor of the state agency on the whistleblower claim was vacated and remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.

 

154 of 1068 DOCUMENTS



Durham v. Peabody Coal Co.


2007-SC-000792-WC, 2007-SC-000793-WC, 2007-SC-000794-WC


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


272 S.W.3d 192; 2008 Ky. LEXIS 240



October 23, 2008, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 22, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Durham v. Peabody Coal Co., 2009 Ky. LEXIS 369 (Ky., Jan. 22, 2009)
Rehearing denied by Middleton v. Centennial Res., Inc., 2009 Ky. LEXIS 373 (Ky., Jan. 22, 2009)
Rehearing denied by Lutz v. Energy Conversion Corp., 2009 Ky. LEXIS 383 (Ky., Jan. 22, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 2007-CA-000032-WC. WORKERS' COMPENSATION BOARD NO. 04-00424.

ON APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 2006-CA-002628-WC. WORKERS' COMPENSATION BOARD NO. 02-02141.

ON APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 2007-CA-000037-WC. WORKERS' COMPENSATION BOARD NO. 02-01784.
Middleton v. Centennial Res., Inc., 2007 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 719 (Ky. Ct. App., Sept. 28, 2007)
Durham v. Peabody Coal Co., 2007 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 624 (Ky. Ct. App., Sept. 28, 2007)
Lutz v. Energy Conversion Corp., 2007 Ky. App. LEXIS 355 (Ky. Ct. App., Sept. 28, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In three consolidated appeals, appellant coal workers sought review of decisions of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which affirmed the denial of their pneumoconiosis claims by the Workers' Compensation Board. The workers claimed that the consensus procedure in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.316 violated equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ky. Const. §§ 1, 2, and 3.


OVERVIEW: Under the procedure in § 342.316(3), the workers and appellee employers each submitted a chest X-ray and a "B" reader's interpretation of the X-ray. Because the parties' reports in each case were not in consensus, the X-rays were then interpreted by a panel of three "B" readers pursuant to § 342.316(3)(b)4.e.; each panel determined the best quality X-ray in evidence was negative. The workers claimed that the consensus procedure discriminated unlawfully between workers who were injured by a harmful occupational exposure to coal dust and those who became physically disabled by a traumatic injury. The court affirmed. The inherent differences in the disease/injuries provided a reasonable basis for the different statutory treatment. Section 342.316(13) did not impose a greater burden of proof than on those workers who claimed benefits under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.730 as the presumption in the consensus procedure was a rebuttable one that could be overcome with clear and convincing evidence. The existence and category of pneumoconiosis were proven with x-ray evidence, but the evidence necessary to prove the existence and extent of a traumatic injury varied with the type of injury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decisions.


 

155 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Parrish v. Commonwealth


2006-SC-000592-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


272 S.W.3d 161; 2008 Ky. LEXIS 338



September 18, 2008, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 22, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE LISABETH HUGHES ABRAMSON, JUDGE. NO. 97-CR-003022.
Parrish v. Commonwealth, 121 S.W.3d 198, 2003 Ky. LEXIS 165 (Ky., 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an inmate with an IQ of 79, was convicted of multiple murders, attempted murder, and robbery, and was sentenced to death. He asserted a post-conviction collateral attack on his sentence under Ky. R. Crim. P. 11.42, alleging in part ineffective assistance of counsel. The Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) denied the motion without an evidentiary hearing and upheld the inmate's sentence. He appealed as a matter of right.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was accused of stabbing his cousin and assaulting her sons after he had spent the day smoking crack cocaine. The court upheld the denial of relief. First, the inmate should have attacked a ruling that he was not exempt from the death penalty because of mental retardation on his direct appeal. Nevertheless, an IQ of 70 was the cut-off for mental retardation in Atkins and Kentucky's statutory scheme for applying Atkins, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 532.130 -.140. Second, counsel conducted a reasonable investigation into his intellectual capacity and introduced sufficient evidence of such during the penalty phase. Third, the jury instructions did not impermissibly limit consideration of his intellectual limitations as mitigating evidence. Fourth, although counsel failed to introduce mitigation evidence from a retained expert about the inmate's lack of future dangerousness in prison, they presented a jail chaplain on that issue. Finally, counsel's failure to introduce evidence of his low intellectual function at a hearing to suppress his police confession was not unreasonable when there was no evidence of police coercion and the law at the time focused on police coercion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order.

Cheyenne Res., Inc. v. Elk Horn Coal Corp.


2006-SC-000721-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


265 S.W.3d 184; 2008 Ky. LEXIS 207



September 18, 2008, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 16, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NUMBER 2005-CA-001901. FLOYD CIRCUIT COURT NO. 97-CI-000634.
Elk Horn Coal Corp. v. Cheyenne Res., Inc., 2006 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 379 (Ky. Ct. App., Sept. 1, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals of Kentucky, which determined that a trial court had incorrectly determined the date from which interest could be calculated on a judgment of restitution.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court rendered a judgment against appellee company in the amount of $9.5 million, plus pre-judgment interest at the rate of 8 % per year, and post-judgment interest in the amount of 12% per year. After the appeals were completed, the trial court entered an order enforcing its judgment which included, pursuant to a 10% penalty for $950,000. In an earlier appeal, the court held that the statutory penalty was unconstitutional and that appellee was entitled to restitution of the $950,000. After remand, the circuit court entered an order for restitution, but did not allow interest on the $950,000. The appellate court reversed, and appellant sought review with the court. The court noted that while the appeals were pending appellant had the unfettered use of $950,000 for over four years and there was nothing in the record that would suggest that there was any equitable reason to require anything other than full restitution. To make appellee whole, appellant needed to pay interest on the $950,000 from the date that it first had use of that money.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court.


 

157 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Benet v. Commonwealth


2006-SC-000422-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


253 S.W.3d 528; 2008 Ky. LEXIS 132



May 22, 2008, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 12, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE MARTIN F. McDONALD, JUDGE. NO. 04-CR-003293.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) convicted defendant of first-degree sodomy and first-degree sexual abuse, and sentenced him to consecutive terms of twenty years' imprisonment and five years' imprisonment, respectively. Thereafter, defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged on appeal that: (1) Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 439.3401 was unconstitutional; (2) the trial court abused its discretion by sentencing him to a more onerous sentence than that recommended by the jury; and (3) his convictions for both sodomy and sexual abuse violated his double jeopardy rights. The appeals court disagreed. First, the constitutional argument was not preserved for appellate review. Likewise, defendant could still be characterized as a violent offender despite the fact that the trial court's final judgment did not specifically designate him as such. Third, the trial court was not required to follow the jury's recommendation as to the method of serving a sentence. Fourth, a reasonable juror could have inferred that the touching of the victim's genitals through the victim's clothing was for the purposes of defendant's own sexual gratification, as he had previously orally sodomized the victim. Further, defendant similarly touched other young boys' genitals through their clothing. Finally, his act of touching the victim's genitals was an entirely separate act and offense than his orally sodomizing the victim. Hence, there was no double jeopardy violation.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were affirmed.

King Drugs, Inc. v. Commonwealth


2005-SC-000789-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


250 S.W.3d 643; 2008 Ky. LEXIS 98



April 24, 2008, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 24, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NUMBER 2004-CA-002019. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT NO. 03-CI-00550.
King Drugs, Inc. v. Commonwealth, 2005 Ky. App. LEXIS 240 (Ky. Ct. App., Sept. 2, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: As to a 1986 amendment to former Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 139.472, a statute exempting "prosthetic devices and physical aids" from Kentucky sales and use tax, appellee, the Kentucky Board of Tax Appeals (Board), granted appellant taxpayers an exemption. But, the Franklin Circuit Court and Kentucky Court of Appeals reversed that holding. The taxpayers then sought further review, which was granted, and the instant decision followed.


OVERVIEW: At issue was whether the Kentucky General Assembly intended to add an exemption for all sales of artificial devices prescribed by a licensed physician, or if it intended only to expand somewhat the prior exemption for sales to crippled persons by including not only devices designed and altered for them but also devices prescribed for their particular use as braces, supports, or similar purposes. The instant court agreed with the Board that the 1986 version of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 139.472 was neither ambiguous nor absurd and that it provided an exemption, parallel to the exemption for sales of prescription medicine, for all sales of artificial devices prescribed by a licensed physician. The court also found that the circuit court and the Court of Appeals erred by reading into the exemption limitations which the General Assembly did not impose.


OUTCOME: Both the orders entered by the circuit court and court of appeals were reversed, and the decision of the Board was affirmed.

Fugett v. Commonwealth


2006-SC-000051-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


250 S.W.3d 604; 2008 Ky. LEXIS 111



April 24, 2008, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 24, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE LISABETH HUGHES ABRAMSON, JUDGE. NO. 04-CR-000391.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky), which convicted him of manslaughter in the second degree and tampering with physical evidence and sentenced him to 30 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed the Commonwealth impermissibly used two of its peremptory challenges and that the circuit court erred in denying his motions to strike two jurors for cause. The supreme court held that the circuit court properly applied the three-step process for evaluating defendant's Batson challenge. However, the circuit court abused its discretion in failing to excuse a juror for cause. The juror should have been stricken for cause because he indicated that he would believe the testimony of a police officer simply because he was a police officer, and that police officers had greater credibility in their testimony than other witnesses. The totality of the juror's responses formed a reasonable basis to conclude that he could not consider all the mitigation evidence that the law demanded. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress statements he made to police. The circuit court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress because detectives properly provided defendant with his Miranda warnings before beginning systematic questioning. Defendant made the statements before he was arrested, and he was not in custody prior to his arrest.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed defendant's convictions and sentence and remanded the matter for further proceedings consistent with its opinion.

J.N.R. v. O'Reilly


2007-SC-000175-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


264 S.W.3d 587; 2008 Ky. LEXIS 115

ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NUMBER 2006-CA-002497. JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT NO. 06-CI-503734.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Kentucky Court of Appeals entered a judgment that denied relief to appellants, a wife and husband, who had petitioned for a writ of prohibition to bar the family court from adjudicating the paternity of appellee alleged biological father who claimed to be the father of a baby born to the wife. The wife and husband appealed.

The wife sought dismissal of the petition. However, the family court declined to dismiss the petition. The state supreme court found that the wife and husband did not have to show irreparable injury and lack of an adequate remedy to obtain the writ because they alleged that the family court was acting outside of its jurisdiction. It then found that the alleged father did not have standing to file the petition and the family court lacked jurisdiction under the Uniform Act on Paternity because there was no claim the child had been born out of wedlock given that there was no evidence or allegation that the husband and wife's marital relationship ceased 10 months before the child's birth, as set forth in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 406.011.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the appellate court's judgment and remanded the case to the appellate court for issuance of a writ of prohibition.

 

161 of 1068 DOCUMENTS



Craig & Bishop, Inc. v. Piles


2005-SC-000999-DG AND 2006-SC-000432-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


247 S.W.3d 897; 2008 Ky. LEXIS 61



March 20, 2008, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 10, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NUMBER 2004-CA-001883-MR. JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT NO. 03-CI-007221.
Piles v. Craig & Bishop, Inc., 2006 Ky. LEXIS 206 (Ky., Aug. 17, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) awarded damages to appellee customers on their claims filed under the Kentucky Consumer Protection Act (Act) against appellant, a used car dealer (dealer). On appeal, the Court of Appeals held that the customers qualified as purchasers under the Act, affirmed the punitive damages award, but vacated the common-law fraud verdict and inconvenience damages award. Thus, the dealer sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The dealer asserted as its principal issue on appeal that the jury verdict on the claims filed under the Act had to be overturned because the customers based their claims on an incomplete sale transaction, meaning that they were not purchasers because they never actually purchased goods from the dealer. But, the instant court first found that the jury's verdict on the claims under the Act was proper. Hence, it declined to address the common-law fraud issue. Second, the customers were eligible to bring an action under the Act as purchasers, as they had an equitable interest in the purchased vehicle equal to the value of their trade in, despite the lack of a binding contract. Third, the court declined to make any finding regarding liability for future promises, such as financing guarantees, as the case did not require the court to determine whether any liability for future predictions was possible under the Act and because the issue was not argued to the trial court. Fourth, punitive damages were properly awarded and were not excessive. Finally, the inconvenience awards were not duplicative of the loss of use award. Thus, it was improperly vacated.


OUTCOME: That part of the Court of Appeals' opinion that affirmed the judgment of the trial court was upheld, and the court did not reach the question as to the propriety of the fraud verdict. But, that part of the Court of Appeals' opinion that vacated that portion of the trial court's judgment was reversed. Thus, the trial court's judgment was reinstated entirely.

Commonwealth v. Bishop


2006-SC-000123-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


245 S.W.3d 733; 2008 Ky. LEXIS 37



February 21, 2008, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 13, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. CASE NUMBER 2004-CA-002432-MR. CLAY CIRCUIT COURT NO. 04-CR-00089-001.
Commonwealth v. Bishop, 2006 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 901 (Ky. Ct. App., Jan. 13, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Kentucky Court of Appeals entered a judgment that affirmed the trial court's decision to dismiss indictments charging the first defendant and the second defendant with drug-related offenses. The state supreme court granted the Commonwealth's motion for discretionary review.


OVERVIEW: The city police officer arrested the first defendant and the second defendant for drug-related offenses at a residence located outside the city limits but within the county limits. The first defendant and the second defendant moved to dismiss the indictments filed against them, and claimed that the arrest was unlawful because it was made by a city police officer outside of the city limits. The trial court agreed with the first defendant and the second defendant, and dismissed the indictments. The appellate court agreed with the trial court's decision and affirmed. The state supreme court found that an earlier municipal order, which amended sections of the city's personnel system and provided that city police were to remain within the city limits unless an emergency arose, did not affect the police officer's county-wide arrest powers under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 95.019(1). Rather, the state supreme court found that the municipal order, though valid, was meant to keep police officers in the city and the violation of it did not make the arrests unlawful; instead, the violation of it could subject a city police officer to employment disciplinary action.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the appellate court's judgment, reinstated the indictments, and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

Owens v. Commonwealth


2006-SC-000037-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


244 S.W.3d 83; 2008 Ky. LEXIS 15



January 24, 2008, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 14, 2008.
Vacated by, Remanded by Owens v. Ky., 2009 U.S. LEXIS 3314 (U.S., May 4, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM TAYLOR CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE DOUGHLAS M. GEORGE, JUDGE. NO. 04-CR-00225.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Taylor Circuit Court (Kentucky) of possession of marijuana, of first-degree possession of a controlled substance, and of being a first-degree persistent felony offender, and sentence, following the denial of his suppression motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a passenger in a vehicle driven by a driver, who was arrested for driving with a suspended license, and was found to possess a crack pipe in a search incident to the arrest. Defendant was asked to step outside the vehicle, and was frisked. The state's highest court adopted the automatic companion rule in finding that the frisk was constitutional. A Terry pat-down was more than counterbalanced by the need to protect both the officers and any innocent bystanders from harm. Adoption of the automatic companion rule provided needed bright line guidance to the bench, bar, law enforcement community, and citizens across the Commonwealth as to what was constitutionally permissible. The automatic companion rule was a limited and narrow exception to the exclusionary rule. It applied only when the driver had been lawfully arrested and the passengers had been lawfully expelled in preparation for a lawful search of the vehicle, and allowed an officer to conduct a brief pat-down for weapons (not a full-blown search) of the vehicle's passengers, regardless of whether those passengers' actions or appearance evidenced any independent indicia of dangerousness or suspicion.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Yell v. Commonwealth


2006-SC-000327-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


242 S.W.3d 331; 2007 Ky. LEXIS 286



December 20, 2007, Rendered


NOTICE: TO BE PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 21, 2007.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Yell v. Kentucky, 553 U.S. 1011, 128 S. Ct. 2068, 170 L. Ed. 2d 806, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 3540 (2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at Yell v. Commonwealth, 2013 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 251 (Ky. Ct. App., Mar. 22, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM LOGAN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE TYLER L. GILL, JUDGE. NO. 04-CR-000232.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Logan Circuit Court (Kentucky) of first-degree arson, first-degree assault, second-degree manslaughter, and second-degree persistent felony offender. The trial court sentenced defendant to various terms of imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: After defendant argued with his girlfriend and choked her, she removed two of her children from the trailer home in which she lived with defendant. Upon returning to the trailer to get the two minor children she had with defendant she saw that smoke was coming from the trailer home. One of the children was killed in the fire, while the other child was burned in the fire. On appeal, the court found that (1) the trial court did not err by allowing a dog handler to testify as to alerts by his dog to the presence of accelerants in the trailer, and the jury was able to weigh the testimony against a lab examiner who did not find accelerants in lab tests; (2) the testimony by fire investigators and other witnesses as well as defendant's statements after the fire were sufficient to support a conviction for arson under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 513.020; (3) although it was error under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 421.260(1) to have arrested a witness while she was in Kentucky to testify in the trial, the error did not require reversal; (4) even if there was error at trial in obstructing the view of a child witness and defendant under U.S. Const. amend. VI and Ky. Const. § 11, any error was harmless.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

165 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Shane v. Commonwealth


2006-SC-000096-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


243 S.W.3d 336; 2007 Ky. LEXIS 262



December 20, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 12, 2008.
Appeal after remand at Shane v. Commonwealth, 2011 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 744 (Ky. Ct. App., Oct. 7, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE F. KENNETH CONLIFFE, JUDGE. NO. 04-CR-000977.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of burglary and of being a persistent felony offender in the second degree. Defendant appealed, contending the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) erred in denying his motion to dismiss based on an 11 year delay, and in denying his motion to strike a challenged juror for cause. Defendant requested that the court overrule Morgan v. Commonwealth.


OVERVIEW: The challenged juror's statement that he was "absolutely" pro-police and that he did not believe an officer would lie under oath clearly indicated that a defendant would have little or no chance of challenging an officer's testimony in that juror's mind. Given the reasonable evidence of bias, it was an abuse of discretion not to strike the juror. While a party could reasonably expect to be given all the rights granted to him by state law or rule, he had a certain right to a trial that was fair in its entirety. Ky. R. Crim. P. 9.36 made it mandatory for trial courts to excuse biased jurors for cause when a reasonable person would view the juror as biased. Not removing a biased juror from the venire, and thereby forcing a defendant to forfeit a peremptory strike, prevented defendant from getting the jury he had a right to choose. That violated a substantial right and could never have been harmless error. Finally, the pre-indictment delay was investigative delay, and thus, was not error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed on the peremptory strikes issue, and overruled Morgan v. Commonwealth. The pre-trial delay claim of error was affirmed. The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

Chapman v. Commonwealth


2005-SC-000070-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


265 S.W.3d 156; 2007 Ky. LEXIS 178



August 23, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified August 21, 2008; As Corrected August 29, 2007. As Corrected December 27, 2007.
Released for Publication October 23, 2008.
Modified and rehearing denied by Chapman v. Commonwealth, 2008 Ky. LEXIS 340 (Ky., Aug. 21, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM BOONE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE ANTHONY FROHLICH, JUDGE. NO. 03-CR-00291.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Boone Circuit Court (Kentucky), which convicted defendant on two counts of capital murder, two counts of attempted murder, one count of rape in the first degree, one count of burglary in the first degree, one count of robbery in the first degree, and one count of being a persistent offender in the second degree. The trial court sentenced defendant to death for the two murders.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions arose from the rape and stabbing of a woman and the stabbing of her three small children, two of whom were killed during the crimes. Defendant made an unusual plea agreement with the Commonwealth in which he agreed to plead guilty and volunteered for the death penalty. The trial court accepted the plea agreement and sentenced defendant to death. On appeal, defendant contended that the death penalty was unconstitutional and that he was incompetent to have voluntarily accepted the death penalty. The court reiterated its long-standing conclusion that the death penalty did not violate the Eighth Amendment of the United States Constitution. The court further held that defendant's death sentence was not disproportionate, pursuant to the court's review as required by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.075(3) considering the intentional killing of the two innocent children. The court also held that it was not necessary for defendant's indictment to have enumerated the aggravators against him nor did the trial court err by appointing defendant stand-by counsel after he requested and obtained withdrawal of his appointed counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence.

GE v. Cain


2004-SC-000043-DG, 2005-SC-000242-DGE


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


236 S.W.3d 579; 2007 Ky. LEXIS 173



August 23, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by GE Co. v. Cain, 2007 Ky. LEXIS 349 (Ky., Nov. 21, 2007)
Subsequent appeal at Rehm v. Ford Motor Co., 365 S.W.3d 570, 2011 Ky. App. LEXIS 195 (Ky. Ct. App., 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 2002-CA-001843. JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. NOS. 97-CI-006559, 97-CI-006560 AND 97-CI-006564. ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 2002-CA-001399. JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT NO. 01-CI-001344.
Rehm v. Navistar Int'l, 2005 Ky. App. LEXIS 48 (Ky. Ct. App., Feb. 25, 2005)
Cain v. GE, 2003 Ky. App. LEXIS 325 (Ky. Ct. App., Dec. 19, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two separate cases before the court from the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), plaintiffs, injured workers or the representative of a deceased worker, appealed respective trial court judgments granting summary judgment favor of defendant premises owners. The judgments established that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.690(1) immunized defendants from tort liability for the occupational diseases plaintiffs claimed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs asserted that they, or their decedent, contracted an occupational disease as a result of exposure to asbestos while performing work for defendants. In its judgments, the trial court found in favor of defendants, holding that they were contractors immune from tort liability, that the exclusive remedy provision was not unconstitutional, and that each owner had sufficiently proven that it had secured payment of compensation per Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.340. In one case, the court held that summary judgment in favor of the premises owner was improper because the available evidence inadequately supported the trial court's finding that plaintiffs performed work of a kind that was a regular or recurrent part of the work of that premises owner's business and because documented evidence established workers' compensation coverage. In the second case, the court found that the evidence did not support the trial court's conclusion that plaintiff in that case performed work of a kind that was a regular part of the work of the premises owners' businesses.


OUTCOME: In the first case, the court affirmed the lower court insofar as that defendant was not entitled to judgment as a matter of law but reversed, in part, on the issue concerning proof of coverage. In the second case, the court reversed, in part, holding that certain defendants were not entitled to judgment as a matter of law and affirmed the proof of coverage and constitutionality issues. The court remanded both cases to the trial court.

 

168 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Furnish v. Commonwealth


2004-SC-000387-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


267 S.W.3d 656; 2007 Ky. LEXIS 294



August 23, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
CORRECTED DECEMBER 15, 2008. MODIFIED NOVEMBER 26, 2008.
Related proceeding at Furnish v. Commonwealth, 2008 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1094 (Ky. Ct. App., Aug. 29, 2008)
Rehearing denied by Furnish v. Commonwealth, 2008 Ky. LEXIS 741 (Ky., Nov. 26, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Furnish v. Kentucky, 558 U.S. 831, 130 S. Ct. 65, 175 L. Ed. 2d 48, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 5673 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM KENTON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE DOUGLAS M. STEPHENS, JUDGE. NO. 98-CR-00384.
Furnish v. Commonwealth, 2006 Ky. LEXIS 233 (Ky., Sept. 21, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Kenton Circuit Court (Kentucky) that imposed the death penalty following his capital murder conviction, arguing that the circuit court erred in allowing him to stipulate to certain aggravating factors and that the introduction of a separate murder conviction should have been admissible at his penalty phase retrial because the conviction did not exist at the time of the original penalty phase.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the U.S. Supreme Court's Apprendi and Blakely rulings did not preclude a defendant in the sentencing phase of a capital murder trial from stipulating to aggravating factors; both concerned the propriety of shifting penalty-enhancing factual determinations from the jury to the trial court, and neither prohibited a defendant from stipulating to penalty-enhancing facts. The evil sought to be eliminated by Apprendi and Blakely was nonconsensual judicial factfinding of penalty-enhancing factors, which infringed upon a defendant's right to have a jury find every element of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt, and nothing in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.025 prevented a defendant from stipulating to the existence of aggravating circumstances. Further, the term "prior," as used in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 532.025(1)(b) and 532.055(2)(a), referred to the status of defendant at the time of sentencing, not at the time of the commission of the charged crime. Thus, the Commonwealth could introduce a conviction that was obtained subsequent to the offense for which a defendant was being sentenced because, at the time of sentencing, it had become a "prior" conviction.


OUTCOME: The final judgment imposing the death penalty was affirmed.

Halvorsen v. Commonwealth


2004-SC-000017-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


258 S.W.3d 1; 2007 Ky. LEXIS 177



August 23, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 22, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Halvorsen v. Commonwealth, 2008 Ky. LEXIS 227 (Ky., Aug. 21, 2008)
Rehearing denied by Halvorsen v. Commonwealth, 2008 Ky. LEXIS 593 (Ky., Aug. 21, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE GARY PAYNE, JUDGE. 83-CR-000152-001.
Halvorsen v. Commonwealth, 730 S.W.2d 921, 1986 Ky. LEXIS 322 (Ky., 1986)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the denial of his postconviction motions pursuant to Ky. R. Civ. P. 59.05 and Ky. R. Crim. P. 11.42 entered by the Fayette Circuit Court (Kentucky) in a case where the inmate had been sentenced to death on two murder counts and to life imprisonment on a third murder count. Appellee Commonwealth made a motion to strike certain affidavits attached to the inmate's brief.


OVERVIEW: Initially, the Commonwealth's motion to strike was denied because while the affidavits were executed after the Rule 11.42 hearing, the trial court had granted a motion to supplement the record. On the merits, the court rejected the inmate's argument of ineffective assistance of counsel on several bases. While the inmate claimed that his trial counsel failed to investigate properly, the court held that additional witnesses on the issues of extreme emotional disturbance (EED) and duress would have been cumulative as several witnesses had testified that the inmate had become depressed and begun heavy drug usage following his divorce and that the inmate had been changed by his friendship with and was possibly frightened by his co-defendant. Duress was not a defense to intentional murder under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 501.090, so it was reasonable trial strategy to present such evidence at the penalty stage instead of the guilt/innocence phase. A jury instruction that the Commonwealth was required to prove an absence of EED beyond a reasonable doubt was not required because the presence or absence of EED was a matter of evidence, not an element of the crime of murder.


OUTCOME: The court denied the Commonwealth's motion to strike and affirmed the trial court's denial of postconviction relief.

Brown v. Commonwealth


2005-SC-000078-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


226 S.W.3d 74; 2007 Ky. LEXIS 126



June 21, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication July 12, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 2003-CA-000292. JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT NO. 01-CR-000497.
Brown v. Commonwealth, 2004 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 567 (Ky. Ct. App., Dec. 23, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for possession of a controlled substance in the first degree, operating a motor vehicle on a learner's permit without a licensed operator, and being a persistent felony offender in the first degree. He was sentenced to eighteen years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: During the trial, defense counsel implied that defendant intended to offer perjured testimony. Defense counsel was then allowed to withdraw and leave the courtroom while defendant testified by way of a narrative statement, was cross-examined by the prosecution, and made his own closing statement. The appellate court ruled that defendant had waived his right to counsel when he proceeded against his attorney's advice, and that his attorney had acted properly in not assisting him to present false testimony. On appeal, the court found that defense counsel properly revealed his concern to the trial court pursuant to Ky. Sup. Ct. R. 3.130-1.6, 3.3. However, the trial court erred in permitting defense counsel to leave the courtroom and in advising appellant and counsel that counsel could leave the courtroom during the narrative testimony. By completely leaving the courtroom, in the presence of the jury, counsel telegraphed a problem to the jury, and defendant was unconstitutionally deprived of his right to assistance of counsel. This was compounded by requiring him to make his own closing argument and allowing counsel to return to conduct the sentencing phase.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the action to the trial court for a new trial.

Dunn v. Felty


2005-SC-000295-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


226 S.W.3d 68; 2007 Ky. LEXIS 127



June 21, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication July 12, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 2004-CA-001029-MR. JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT NO. 01-CI-002368.
Dunn v. Felty, 2005 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 80 (Ky. Ct. App., Apr. 1, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant arrestee sued appellee police officer for false imprisonment and the use of excessive force. The trial court dismissed the claims as time-barred under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 413.140(1)(a), (c); the Kentucky Court of Appeals affirmed. The arrestee sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Police went to the arrestee's condominium complex to investigate a complaint. The arrestee alleged he approached an officer due to worries about his stepdaughter, and that the officer choked him, struck him with a flashlight, and excessively tightened his handcuffs. Based on this incident, the arrestee was charged with menacing, resisting arrest, and harassment; he was acquitted on all counts. Less than a year after his acquittal, he filed the instant suit. The trial court held the false imprisonment and excessive force claims were barred by § 413.140(1)(a), (c) because the arrestee filed suit more than a year after his arrest. The high court held that as the favorable termination of criminal proceedings was not an element of false imprisonment, the limitations period began to run on the false imprisonment claim when the alleged false imprisonment ended, which occurred when the arrestee was arraigned on the charges. As he did not file suit within one year of his release from custody, his false imprisonment claim was time-barred. And as his excessive force claim accrued at the time of injury, but he filed suit more than one year after the arrest, that claim was also time-barred.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed.

Colwell v. Dresser Instrument Div.


2006-SC-0048-WC


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


217 S.W.3d 213; 2006 Ky. LEXIS 297



November 22, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 27, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Colwell v. Dresser Instrument Div., 2007 Ky. LEXIS 99 (Ky., Apr. 19, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS 2005-CA-1452-WC. WORKERS' COMPENSATION NO. 99-72338.
Dresser Instrument Div. v. Colwell, 2005 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 453 (Ky. Ct. App., Dec. 9, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant worker sought to reopen her settled workers' compensation claim. The Court of Appeals (Kentucky) reversed a decision by the workers' compensation board, and ruled that the finding of the administrative law judge (ALJ) on the issue of impairment was a sufficient basis to dismiss the reopening. The worker appealed.


OVERVIEW: The ALJ relied on a physician who testified that the 12 percent impairment rating which was the basis for the initial settlement had not changed, and that the only change at reopening was in the worker's subjective complaints of pain. The appellate court ruled that, because Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.125(1)(d) required only a "worsening of impairment," the worker was not required to prove a greater permanent impairment rating in order to receive permanent total disability benefits at reopening. Her burden was to prove by objective medical evidence that she sustained a worsening of impairment from the injury, to prove that the change was permanent, and to prove that it caused her to be totally and permanently disabled under the standard described in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.0011(11)(c). The worker was entitled to receive the difference between the actual disability the injury caused at settlement and the disability that it caused at reopening. Because it was not entirely clear that the ALJ applied the correct standard when determining whether the worker experienced a worsening of impairment, the claim needed to be remanded for further consideration.


OUTCOME: The decision of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed in part and reversed in part, and the claim is remanded to the ALJ for further consideration.

Commonwealth v. Jameson


2004-SC-000983-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


215 S.W.3d 9; 2006 Ky. LEXIS 290



November 22, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication April 2, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Commonwealth v. Jameson, 2007 Ky. LEXIS 75 (Ky., Mar. 22, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Jameson v. Kentucky, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 9107 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 2003-CA-000967-DG. MCCRACKEN CIRCUIT COURT, NOS. 00-M-01796, 00-M-01797 AND 02-XX-00004.
Jameson v. Commonwealth, 2004 Ky. App. LEXIS 229 (Ky. Ct. App., Aug. 6, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was cited for operating an adult cabaret in violation of McCracken County, Ky., Ordinance No. 2000-4, filed a motion to declare the ordinance unconstitutional. The district court denied the motion. A circuit court affirmed the district court. The Kentucky Court of Appeals affirmed the decision in part, vacated the decision in part, and remanded the case for further proceedings. The Commonwealth of Kentucky appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Fiscal Court for McCracken County, Kentucky enacted McCracken County, Ky., Ordinance No. 2000-4 to prevent the negative secondary effects generally associated with sexually oriented businesses. Defendant filed a First Amendment challenge to the ordinance. The Kentucky Supreme Court found that the Court of Appeals erred in vacating part of the holding of the district court because (1) the ordinance was within the constitutional power of the county to enact under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 67.083(3)(z); (2) the ordinance was content neutral as the government's interest in preventing negative secondary effects associated with sexually oriented businesses was unrelated to the suppression of expression; (3) the ordinance furthered the county's substantial governmental interest in preventing and combating the negative secondary effects associated with sexually oriented businesses; and (4) the requirements of the ordinance were only a minimal restriction in furtherance of the asserted government interests. Moreover, defendant did not present sufficient evidence to cast doubt on the fiscal court's rationale or findings, and thus shift the evidentiary burden back to the fiscal court.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Court of Appeals was reversed insofar as it remanded the case to the district court for further evidentiary hearings and required the fiscal court to proffer supplementary evidence in support of the ordinance. The prior holding of the district court regarding the constitutionality of the ordinance was reinstated.

Williams v. Commonwealth


2003-SC-0319-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


213 S.W.3d 671; 2006 Ky. LEXIS 305



November 22, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 13, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Williams v. Commonwealth, 2007 Ky. LEXIS 49 (Ky., Feb. 22, 2007)
Related proceeding at Williams v. Ky. Bd. of Med. Licensure, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 69853 (W.D. Ky., Sept. 11, 2008)
Related proceeding at Williams v. Ky. Bd. of Med. Licensure, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 105961 (W.D. Ky., Oct. 4, 2010)
Appeal after remand at Williams v. Commonwealth, 2011 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 301 (Ky. Ct. App., Apr. 8, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM LEWIS CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE LEWIS D. NICHOLLS, JUDGE. 02-CR-00029.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of four counts of unlawfully prescribing a controlled substance, in violation of Ky. Rev. Stat. § 218A.1404(3). The Lewis Circuit Court (Kentucky) sentenced him to 20 years' imprisonment. Defendant challenged the judgment of conviction.


OVERVIEW: The evidence seized during a warrantless raid of defendant's medical clinic should have been excluded as violative of the Fourth Amendment and Ky. Const. § 10 where criminal law enforcement investigators had supplied the information upon which the raid was based and had determined which files were to be seized by the medical board. Moreover, a short delay in obtaining a warrant would not have frustrated the governmental authorities involved in the case. However, the statement made by defendant to two agents did not need to be suppressed as fruit of the poisonous tree where the statements were made voluntarily and without any intimidation or coercion and defendant was not seized or detained at the time he was questioned. Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.202(6)(a) and (b) were facially constitutional as the examination of the Kentucky All-Schedule Prescription Electronic Reporting System reports did not constitute a search under the Fourth Amendment or Ky. Const. § 10. The convictions did not offend double jeopardy principles where each prescription for a controlled substance was a specific period of conduct constituting a separate offense under Ky. Rev. Stat. § 218A.1404(3).


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was vacated. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

Sublett v. Commonwealth


NO. 2005-SC-000832-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


203 S.W.3d 701; 2006 Ky. LEXIS 257



October 19, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 20, 2006.
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Sublett v. Motley, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 105550 (W.D. Ky., Mar. 4, 2008)
Review denied by Sublett v. Commonwealth, 2010 Ky. LEXIS 624 (Ky., Sept. 15, 2010)
Post-conviction relief denied at Sublett v. Commonwealth, 2012 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 469 (Ky. Ct. App., July 13, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE LISABETH HUGHES ABRAMSON, JUDGE. INDICTMENT NOS. 03-CR-002331, 03-CR-003102, AND 05-CR-000556.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following the denial of defendant's motion to suppress, defendant pleaded guilty to 21 counts of first-degree robbery, expressly reversing the right to appeal the denial of the motion to suppress. The Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) sentenced defendant to 25 years in prison in accordance with the plea agreement. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred by denying the motion to suppress evidence obtained in two searches conducted at the respective homes of defendant's mother and sister. The appellate court held that the trial court's factual finding that defendant's mother consented to the entry of her home was conclusive, as it was supported by substantial evidence. The appellate court also concluded that the parole officers had the authority to arrest defendant. The search of defendant's sister house was not erroneous either, but was justified by the plain language of the conditions of defendant's release on parole. Defendant also argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress statements made to police interrogators following defendant's arrest. The appellate court disagreed, concluding that the trial court properly exercised its discretion to judge the credibility of witnesses and to draw inferences from their testimony. The trial court accepted the testimony of several police officers that defendant did not invoke his rights before making statements and rejected defendant's testimony to the contrary.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

177 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Furnish v. Commonwealth


2004-SC-0387-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


2006 Ky. LEXIS 233



September 21, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing granted by Furnish v. Commonwealth, 2007 Ky. LEXIS 544 (Ky., Jan. 25, 2007)
Substituted opinion at, On rehearing at Furnish v. Commonwealth, 267 S.W.3d 656, 2007 Ky. LEXIS 294 (Ky., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM KENTON CIRCUIT COURT. 1998-CR-0384-MR. HONORABLE DOUGLAS M. STEPHENS, JUDGE.
Furnish v. Commonwealth, 95 S.W.3d 34, 2002 Ky. LEXIS 221 (Ky., 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death, the present court remanded the case for a new penalty phase where defendant would be eligible for an instruction on life without parole. On remand, a different jury in the Kenton Circuit Court (Kentucky) recommended a death sentence, and the trial court again sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court first held that the trial court did not err in determining that aggravating circumstances had been found by the first jury and that defendant had stipulated to the existence of the aggravating circumstances. An aggravating circumstance could be found in either the guilt or the penalty phase, and Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.025 did not prevent a defendant from stipulating to the existence of aggravating circumstances. Next, the sentence of life without parole defendant had received for an earlier murder did not estop the Commonwealth from seeking the death penalty in the present case. Even if the doctrine applied, defendant had not shown the elements necessary to establish estoppel. A prosecutor's asking a defense witness if she had e-mailed defendant or had checked his web site was not an improper comment on the amenities in prison. The prosecutor's use of the term "evil" and the phrase "a leopard cannot change its spots" in closing was not improper, given defense counsel's comment that defendant was traveling "the road to redemption." Defendant had already been found guilty. Finally, the court had previously held that lethal injection was not cruel and unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the jury in regard to the penalty phase.

Roberie v. VonBokern


2004-SC-000250-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


2006 Ky. LEXIS 186



August 24, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Roberie v. Vonbokern, 2006 Ky. LEXIS 544 (Ky., Dec. 21, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 2002-CA-001940-MR. OWEN CIRCUIT COURT NO. 99-CI-00124.
Roberie v. Vonbokern, 2004 Ky. App. LEXIS 59 (Ky. Ct. App., Mar. 5, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a husband and wife, challenged a judgment which determined that a dirt road was a public road and awarded punitive damages to the primary appellees, neighbors, based on appellants' acts in denying road access to the neighbors. The Court of Appeals (Kentucky) remanded the case for further consideration of the punitive damages award and otherwise affirmed. The state supreme court granted appellants' motion for discretionary review.


OVERVIEW: The disputed unpaved dirt road formed a border between the parties' properties. Although the neighbors' property was not landlocked, the disputed road provided the best access to the northern section of their farm. Eventually, the parties became embroiled in a dispute over access to the road. Appellants erected fenceposts at the entrance to the road, completely blocking access. The jury found that the disputed road was in fact a county road and awarded punitive damages of $ 5,000 to the neighbors, presumably for appellants' intimidating, abusive behavior and for blocking access to the road. The state supreme court held that the neighbors' claim was valid and amounted to a private action for a public nuisance. The neighbors alleged that the disputed dirt road was actually a public turnpike that was owned by the county and that appellants' efforts to prevent their access to the road amounted to an interference with a public right. While appellants' conduct was not so reprehensible as to support unlimited punitive damages, the appellate court could not say that the award of $ 5,000 was so out of step with the degree of reprehensibility as to be unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The decision by the appellate court to remand the case to the trial court for further consideration of the punitive damages award was reversed. The remainder of the judgment was affirmed.


 

179 of 1068 DOCUMENTS



Storm v. Mullins


2006-SC-000008-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


199 S.W.3d 156; 2006 Ky. LEXIS 204



August 24, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified August 25, 2006.
 [**1] Released for Publication September 28, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 2005-CA-000647. FLOYD CIRCUIT COURT NO. 02-AD-0007.
Storm v. Mullins, 2005 Ky. App. LEXIS 262 (Ky. Ct. App., Dec. 9, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Ky. R. Civ. P. 60.02, appellant mother filed a motion to set aside a judgment of adoption in favor of appellee paternal grandparents, the adoptive parents of her two minor children. The Floyd Circuit Court, Family Court Division (Kentucky), denied the motion on grounds it was untimely under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 199.540(2); the Kentucky Court of Appeals affirmed. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The children were raised primarily by their grandparents, without any objection by the mother. Two and one-half years after the adoption judgment was entered, she filed the instant action, alleging she never signed a consent to adoption and was never served with a copy of the adoption petition. She had signed a "consent to custody" form that did not mention adoption and did not include the information required by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 199.011(14) to be included in adoption consent forms. The appellate court held that as she failed to challenge the adoption within a year after entry of the judgment, her challenge based on the failure to comply with the statutory adoption procedures was barred by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 199.540(2)'s one-year limitation period. But if, as she alleged, she had lacked adequate notice of adoption proceedings, strict application of § 199.540(2) might violate her Fourteenth Amendment due process rights. Due to the state of the record, remand was required to determine whether she had sufficient notice of the adoption proceedings. If she had received notice of the proceedings but failed to appear or raise any objection, then she waived any due process claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was reversed, and the case was remanded to the trial court for additional factfinding.


 

180 of 1068 DOCUMENTS



Baker v. Fletcher


2005-SC-000208-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


204 S.W.3d 589; 2006 Ky. LEXIS 153; 152 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P60,221



June 15, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 22, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Baker v. Fletcher, 2006 Ky. LEXIS 328 (Ky., Nov. 22, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON TRANSFER FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. 2005-CA-0613. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT NO. 04-CI-01169.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky) entered a judgment that determined the General Assembly had the authority to retroactively suspend Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18A.355, which was a statute that provided all employees of the Commonwealth an annual increment in their salaries of not less than five percent. Appellant state employees appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state employees filed a class action complaint in the trial court and requested declaratory and injunctive relief against appellee governor, in his official capacity as Kentucky's governor, after a failure to enact a comprehensive balanced budget appropriating revenues to fund the Executive Branch occurred. The result of the alleged failure was that the governor issued an executive order giving state employees a 2.7 percent annual raise despite the fact that they were entitled to at least a five percent annual increment pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18A.355. The trial court found that the General Assembly could retroactively suspend Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18A.355. On appeal, the state supreme court found that the governor did not have the power to suspend statutes but that the General Assembly had such a power. Moreover, the state supreme court found that the General Assembly could retroactively suspend statutes, pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 446.080(3), if the legislature clearly manifested its intent to do so and the evidence showed that the General Assembly had intended such a result by the language it used in bills that it passed regarding the budget.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.


 

181 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Bowling v. Commonwealth


2005-SC-0712-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


224 S.W.3d 577; 2006 Ky. LEXIS 159



June 15, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication June 21, 2007.
Later proceeding at Baze v. Rees, 217 S.W.3d 207, 2006 Ky. LEXIS 301 (Ky., 2006)
Rehearing denied by Bowling v. Commonwealth, 2007 Ky. LEXIS 137 (Ky., June 21, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Bowling v. Kentucky, 552 U.S. 1152, 128 S. Ct. 1090, 169 L. Ed. 2d 827, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 844 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE MARY C. NOBLE, JUDGE. 1990-CR-0363.
Bowling v. Commonwealth, 163 S.W.3d 361, 2005 Ky. LEXIS 95 (Ky., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of two murders and was sentenced to death. Pursuant to Ky. R. Civ. P. 60.02 and 60.03, he filed a motion to vacate his death sentence based upon "juvenile mental age." The Fayette Circuit Court (Kentucky) denied him relief; he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate exhausted his state court appeals, and his federal habeas petition, which alleged he could not be executed because he was mentally retarded, was unsuccessful. The trial court found that he failed to present evidence sufficient for it to determine the scientific validity of "mental age." On appeal, he argued that under the rationale of Roper v. Simmons, which was decided after his trial, the execution of offenders whose mental age was below 18 violated the Eight Amendment's ban on cruel and unusual punishment. The high court disagreed. Roper prohibited the execution of only those offenders whose chronological age was below 18 at the time of the commission of the offense. Moreover, a decision recognizing a new constitutional right would not be retroactively applied if a statute in effect at the time of trial afforded the same right. As Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 640.040 barred the execution of offenders under 16, Roper created no greater protection than § 640.040, and the inmate's claim, even if viable, was procedurally defaulted.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was affirmed.

 

182 of 1068 DOCUMENTS



Spears v. Carhartt, Inc.


2005-SC-0694-WC


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


215 S.W.3d 1; 2006 Ky. LEXIS 126; 179 L.R.R.M. 3019



May 18, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 2, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Spears v. Carhartt, Inc., 2007 Ky. LEXIS 73 (Ky., Mar. 22, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 2004-CA-0623-WC. WORKERS' COMPENSATION NO. 97-63991.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.277 and a collective bargaining agreement (CBA), a workers' compensation claim was submitted for alternative dispute resolution (ADR), appellee arbitrator determined after a hearing that appellant claimant's request for arbitration was untimely under the CBA. Appellee Kentucky Workers' Compensation Board and the Kentucky Court of Appeals affirmed. The claimant sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The claimant hurt her back at work; her claim was referred to mediation under the ADR agreement. She told the mediator she rejected appellant employer's settlement offer and needed to talk to her attorney. About 14 months later, her attorney demanded arbitration. The arbitrator dismissed her claim for permanent income benefits, finding the request for arbitration - which, under the ADR agreement, had to be filed within 30 days after the mediation concluded -- was unreasonably late. The claimant argued that the ADR agreement violated Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.277(3) by diminishing her rights, and denied her procedural due process and the same rights to income benefits and notice as provided in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. ch. 342. The high court disagreed. She was aware of the ADR program and had ample time to obtain advice from counsel as to her rights. As she continued in her job after her union agreed to the ADR provision, she was deemed to have consented to it and was properly charged with knowledge of its terms. Though the delay in requesting arbitration did not affect the employer's ability to defend, permitting a such a delay would have increased its interest costs on unpaid benefits.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

183 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Moore v. Commonwealth


2004-SC-0550-DG, 2004-SC-0552-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


199 S.W.3d 132; 2006 Ky. LEXIS 135



May 18, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 28, 2006.
Post-conviction relief denied at Hawkins v. Commonwealth, 2007 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 206 (Ky. Ct. App., Dec. 14, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 2003-CA-751. DAVIESS CIRCUIT COURT. 97-CR-235, 97-CR-344 AND 97-CR-356. ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 2003-CA-1394. WOLFE CIRCUIT COURT. 97-CR-26.
Hawkins v. Commonwealth, 2004 Ky. LEXIS 259 (Ky., Oct. 13, 2004)
Moore v. Commonwealth, 2002 Ky. App. LEXIS 1724 (Ky. Ct. App., Aug. 16, 2002)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING NO. 2004-SC-0550-DG, AND REVERSING AND REMANDING NO. 2004-SC-0552-DG


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two separate cases, appellants filed motions for belated appeals from motions filed under Ky. R. Crim. P. 11.42. The Court of Appeals (Kentucky) denied the motions in each case and overruled motions to reconsider its orders. Appellants filed appeals against appellee Commonwealth of Kentucky, and the court addressed the appeals in a single opinion.


OVERVIEW: The first appellant had been appointed an attorney to assist him with his appeal from his motion. The attorney mailed the notice of appeal to the wrong court. The court stated that when incompetence of state-appointed counsel cost an indigent defendant a right of appeal under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22A.020(1), that defendant ought to be entitled to a belated appeal. Thus, the court rejected the dictum in Merrick v. Commonwealth, 132 S.W.3d 220, 221 (Ky. App. 2004), that suggested that a reinstated or belated appeal was never available except in a direct first appeal of a judgment of conviction. The second appellant, however, was not represented by counsel when he filed his late appeal, and his motion for a belated appeal was properly denied. The second appellant also argued that the notice of the entry of the order denying relief under Ky. R. Crim. P. 11.42 had been served upon him incorrectly and thus the time for appeal would not start to run until it was corrected. The court rejected this argument. There was an entry as required by Ky. R. Crim. P. 12.06(2), and the second appellant did not deny that he had been served with proper notice of the date the judgment was entered.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's decision as to the first appellant and remanded the case with instructions for the lower court to grant his motion for belated appeal. It affirmed the lower court's decision as to the second appellant.

 

184 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Matheney v. Commonwealth


2002-SC-0920-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


191 S.W.3d 599; 2006 Ky. LEXIS 66



March 23, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 15, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Matheney v. Commonwealth, 2006 Ky. LEXIS 613 (Ky., June 15, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Matheney v. Kentucky, 549 U.S. 1057, 127 S. Ct. 667, 166 L. Ed. 2d 522, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 9094 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM HOPKINS CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE CHARLES W. BOTELER, JR., JUDGE. 01-CR-123.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Hopkins Circuit Court (Kentucky) for manufacturing methamphetamine and being a persistent felony offender in the second degree. Defendant argued that since he did not possess all the chemicals necessary to manufacture methamphetamine, his conviction had to be reversed pursuant to Kotila.


OVERVIEW: A store manager recognized defendant as having bought two boxes of Sudafed three weeks earlier and called the police. Defendant's trunk was subsequently found to contain 396 cold and allergy pills containing ephedrine or pseudoephedrine, a gallon of Liquid Fire, and three cans of Pyro. The appellate court held that Kotila's construction of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.1432(1)(b) was incorrect. The language in § 218A.1432(1)(b) that stated "the chemicals or equipment for the manufacture of methamphetamine" meant that one had to possess two or more chemicals or items of equipment with the intent to manufacture methamphetamine to fall within the statute. Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.1432(1)(b) was not unconstitutionally vague. The manager's testimony showed defendant's intent to manufacture methamphetamine; thus, it was admissible. While the prosecutor technically misstated the law, regarding the intent element, since the trial court correctly instructed the jury, the error did not rise to flagrant misconduct.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.
