Epperson v. Commonwealth


2003-SC-0595-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


197 S.W.3d 46; 2006 Ky. LEXIS 49



February 23, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 24, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Epperson v. Commonwealth, 2006 Ky. LEXIS 785 (Ky., Aug. 24, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Epperson v. Kentucky, 549 U.S. 1290, 127 S. Ct. 1840, 167 L. Ed. 2d 337, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 3185 (2007)
Writ of mandamus granted Hodge v. Coleman, 244 S.W.3d 102, 2008 Ky. LEXIS 14 (Ky., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM WARREN CIRCUIT COURT. 1997-CR-0016. HONORABLE THOMAS R. LEWIS.
Hodge v. Commonwealth, 68 S.W.3d 338, 2001 Ky. LEXIS 159 (Ky., 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Warren Circuit Court (Kentucky) of two counts of complicity to murder, first-degree robbery, and first-degree burglary. Defendant was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court abused its discretion when it declined to excuse for cause a prospective juror who could not consider a minimum sentence for the offense of intentional murder, and accordingly, he was deprived of his right to due process. The supreme court disagreed. The juror was ultimately removed from the panel by a peremptory challenge by the defense. A review of all of the answers given by the prospective juror during voir dire indicated her willingness to consider a minimum sentence. The juror was questioned by both prosecution and defense and in response to questions by defense counsel indicated that she would have to listen to the evidence in the case. She stated that she could consider a term of years depending on the facts of the case. A subsequent request for removal of the juror by the defense was denied by the trial court. An analysis of the answers given by the juror during voir dire indicated that there was sufficient basis for her to express her willingness not to automatically vote for the death penalty and to consider the full range of penalties.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

186 of 1068 DOCUMENTS



Krahwinkel v. Commonwealth Aluminum Corp.


2003-SC-0708-DG AND 2004-SC-0219-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


183 S.W.3d 154; 2005 Ky. LEXIS 394



August 25, 2005, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
As Modified February 23, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW AND CROSS-REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 2002-CA-124 AND 2002-CA-193. HANCOCK CIRCUIT COURT NO. 97-CI-4.
Krahwinkel v. Commonwealth Aluminum Corp., 2005 Ky. LEXIS 238 (Ky., Aug. 25, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an employee of an independent contractor, sued appellee owner of an industrial plant, seeking damages arising from appellant's fall at the plant. A jury returned a verdict finding both parties at fault and fixing the injured person's damages at $ 44,971. The trial court reduced the judgment to a lump sum of $ 33,728. The Court of Appeals (Kentucky) reversed and vacated the judgment. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner had contracted with appellant's employer to buy a system which required installation of a large tank at the plant. While working on the project, appellant fell and was injured. Appellant alleged that the owner was negligent in various ways. The intermediate appellate court held that an owner was not liable for injuries to third parties arising out of work performed by an independent contractor unless the work was a nuisance or is inherently dangerous, and that the work at issue fell into neither of those categories. The intermediate appellate court also held that, in any event, the owner's liability was limited to payment of workers' compensation benefits. The appellate court found that the cases relied on to vacate the judgment were inapplicable since they addressed an owner's vicarious liability for injuries caused by the contractor's negligence. The trial court properly held the owner liable because of the owner's own negligence. Finally, the language in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.700(1) clearly precluded double recovery by appellant and did not condition that preclusion upon whether his employer actually pursued its subrogation right.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was reversed insofar as it vacated appellant's judgment in its entirety, and the case was remanded to the trial court with directions to determine an appropriate computation of the total credit due to the owner in light of the employer's/insurer's failure to assert its right of subrogation and enter an amended judgment in accordance with that computation.

Posey v. Commonwealth


2004-SC-0060-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


185 S.W.3d 170; 2006 Ky. LEXIS 53



February 23, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Posey v. Ky., 2006 U.S. LEXIS 6540 (U.S., Oct. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. 02-CA-2519-MR. JEFFERSON CIRCUIT NO. 02-CR-000505.
Posey v. Commonwealth, 2004 Ky. LEXIS 294 (Ky., Nov. 10, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss firearm charges based on the purported unconstitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 527.040 and his motion to suppress evidences. After entering conditional guilty pleas to trafficking in marijuana, possession of a firearm by a convicted felon, and possession of a controlled substance and drug paraphernalia, he appealed. The Kentucky Court of Appeals affirmed; defendant sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Attempting to serve an arrest warrant on another person, police went to defendant's home. While talking to him on the porch, they saw shotgun shells and packets of marijuana inside the home and smelled an odor of marijuana. The police entered the home through the open door, arrested him for possession of a controlled substance, and seized the marijuana and shotgun shells. They searched the home and found a gun, electronic scales, and codeine cough syrup. The high court held that as exigent circumstances justified entry into the home in order to prevent the imminent destruction of evidence, defendant's Fourth Amendment rights were not violated. That possession of marijuana (Ky. Rev. Stat. § 218A.1422) was a misdemeanor was immaterial as defendant faced up to one year's imprisonment if convicted. He argued that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 527.040, which prohibited convicted felons from possessing guns, violated the right to bear arms guaranteed by Ky. Const. § 1(7). The high court disagreed. The right to bear arms set forth in Ky. Const. § 1(7) was not absolute. Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 527.040 was not arbitrary or irrational and did not unduly infringe upon the people's right to bear arms.


OUTCOME: The high court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals.

Stephenson v. Woodward


2005-SC-0603-TG, 2005-SC-0604-TG, 2005-SC-0645-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


182 S.W.3d 162; 2005 Ky. LEXIS 391



December 22, 2005, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 17, 2006.
Released for Publication January 19, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON TRANSFER FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 2005-CA-1601-MR. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT NO. 2004-CI-1676.

ON TRANSFER FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 2005-CA-1602-MR. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT NO. 2004-CI-1676.

ON TRANSFER FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 2005-CA-1643-MR. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT NO. 2004-CI-1676.
Stephenson v. Woodward, 190 S.W.3d 317, 2005 Ky. LEXIS 395 (Ky., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky) granted summary judgment in favor of appellee candidate, and against appellants, the candidate's opponent and the president of the state senate, holding that the opponent was not qualified to hold the office of state senator for the 37th District. The court also denied the candidate's request for an injunction. The opponent and president appealed, while the candidate cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The gravamen of the arguments posed by both the opponent and the resident was that Ky. Const. § 2 did not permit the judiciary to review the General Assembly's exercise of power pursuant to Ky. Const. § 38 and, therefore, the Franklin Circuit Court erred in holding that the senate acted arbitrarily in seating the candidate as state senator. But, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 118.176 clearly permitted a circuit court to consider and adjudicate challenges to a candidate's bona fides commenced prior to the general election. Also, there were no limitations placed on how far in advance of the election the action had to be commenced, nor were there limitations placed on the circuit court concerning the time for adjudication. Further, the Jefferson Circuit Court had jurisdiction to adjudicate the candidate's motion and grant her relief, and that jurisdiction continued after the election occurred. Finally, the circuit court did not err in declining to compel the president to seat the candidate as the senator for the 37th District, and, the fact that her opponent was disqualified did not grant her a right to the office. Rather, the effect was that no election occurred.


OUTCOME: Although a portion of the judgment was reversed, that portion declaring that the opponent was not constitutionally qualified for the office of State Senator and could not be seated was affirmed, as was that part of the judgment denying the candidate's request to compel the Senate to seat her.

Hilltop Basic Res., Inc. v. County of Boone


2003-SC-1052-DG and 2004-SC-0003-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


180 S.W.3d 464; 2005 Ky. LEXIS 390



December 22, 2005, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 12, 2006.
On remand at Hilltop Basic Res., Inc. v. County of Boone, 2006 Ky. App. LEXIS 113 (Ky. Ct. App., Apr. 14, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 2002-CA-001081. BOONE CIRCUIT NO. 00-CI-01144.
Hilltop Basic Res., Inc. v. County of Boone, 2003 Ky. App. LEXIS 250 (Ky. Ct. App., Oct. 10, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought a zoning amendment for purposes of underground mining. The trial court affirmed a decision of the Fiscal Court, which rejected a recommendation of the planning commission of appellee county and denied the application for the zoning amendment. The Court of Appeals (Kentucky) reversed. The corporation appealed and the county cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The intermediate appellate court held that prejudgment and bias by two Fiscal Court members operated to deprive the corporation of procedural due process. The appellate court disagreed. In the administrative or legislative context, the concept of impartiality was, by necessity and by function, more relaxed and informal. Zoning determinations were only subject to judiciary review for the limited purpose of considering whether such determinations were arbitrary. Under the circumstances of this case, the corporation's right to receive fair and nonarbitrary treatment before the Fiscal Court was adequately protected by adhering to the traditional standards. There were no allegations of malice, fraud, corruption, or other conflicts of interest on the part of the Fiscal Court members. Moreover, despite the members' preexisting opinions regarding the community effects of subsurface mining in general, nothing in the record indicated that these members did not seriously or honestly consider the corporation's proposal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.


 

190 of 1068 DOCUMENTS



Keith v. Hopple Plastics


2004-SC-0451-WC


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


178 S.W.3d 463; 2005 Ky. LEXIS 369



November 23, 2005, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 14, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 2003-CA-1129-WC. WORKERS' COMPENSATION BOARD NO. 00-81283.
Keith v. Hopple Plastics, 2004 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 881 (Ky. Ct. App., May 7, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee appealed a judgment by the Court of Appeals (Kentucky) that affirmed a decision by appellee Workers' Compensation Board denying her application for benefits; the employee claimed that Ky. Rev. Stat. § 342.730(4) (1996) violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment and/or Ky. Const. § 3.


OVERVIEW: The employee's work-related injury occurred when she was 68 years old and eligible for Social Security retirement benefits. An administrative law judge determined that Ky. Rev. Stat. § 342.730(4) (1996) limited the duration of the employee's partial disability award to 27.57 weeks. The employee asserted that she was entitled to receive 425 weeks of partial disability benefits. She argued that because the purpose of partial disability benefits was to compensate her for having received a permanent injury, the General Assembly had no rational basis for treating her differently based on her age. The state supreme court found that the employee's argument was based on the erroneous premise that benefits awarded for total and partial disability had different purposes. The employee failed to show that § 342.730(4) had no conceivable rational basis. Consequently, because the constitutionality of the statute had been previously upheld, the employee's equal protection arguments under the Fourteenth Amendment and Ky. Const. § 3 failed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Wood v. Commonwealth


2003-SC-0535-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


178 S.W.3d 500; 2005 Ky. LEXIS 367



November 23, 2005, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Modified December 1, 2005. Released for Publication December 14, 2005.
Post-conviction relief denied at Wood v. Commonwealth, 2012 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 506 (Ky. Ct. App., July 27, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM BARREN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JOHN D. MINTON, JR., SPECIAL JUDGE. 2001-CR-0059.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Barren Circuit Court (Kentucky), which convicted defendant of capital murder and kidnapping, kidnapping, first-degree criminal trespass, second-degree assault, and violation of a protective order. Defendant was sentenced to life without the benefit of parole for the capital charges, 20 years for the kidnapping, 12 months for the trespass charge, and other terms for the other offenses.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions arose from shooting his ex-girlfriend, shooting a male companion of the ex-girlfriend, and defendant holding an innocent homeowner hostage in a three hour standoff with police. After shooting his ex-girlfriend, defendant took her to his car and drove away with her legs dragging from the rear passenger door. On appeal, defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to have supported the jury's determination that the ex-girlfriend was murdered during the course of a kidnapping since she had died when shot. The court noted that the jury implicitly determined that the ex-girlfriend was alive at the time defendant took her from her vehicle because one can kidnap only a living person. Further, the testimony of an expert physician was that the ex-girlfriend would not have died instantly, which provided enough evidence upon which the jury could have based its conclusion. The court found no merit in defendant attempting to launch a collateral attack on the validity of the emergency protective order that had been granted to the ex-girlfriend previously and no abuse of discretion was found for denying defendant's change of venue request.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

192 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Hayes v. Commonwealth


2003-SC-0675-MR; 2003-SC-0717-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


175 S.W.3d 574; 2005 Ky. LEXIS 332



October 20, 2005, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 10, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM GRAYSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE SAM MONARCH, JUDGE. 01-CR-109.

APPEAL FROM GRAYSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE SAM MONARCH, JUDGE. 01-CR-112.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Grayson Circuit Court, Kentucky, after a jury trial, convicted two defendants of manufacturing methamphetamine, that was firearm enhanced, and possession of anhydrous ammonia in an unapproved container with intent to manufacture methamphetamine. One defendant was also convicted of possession of drug paraphernalia, subsequent offense, and receiving stole property. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The dispositive issue was if the trial court committed reversible error when it denied defendants their right to ascertain during voir dire if any prospective juror would be prejudiced against them if they exercised their Fifth Amendment rights not to testify in their own defense. Each defendant exercised that Fifth Amendment right. The trial court opened juror voir dire with a series of questions. The State's prosecutor followed. Defendants' counsel followed the prosecutor. The trial court prohibited counsel from asking certain questions because it said its "no adverse inference" jury instructions would cure any prejudice. Counsel's questions were whether a juror understood defendants did not have to testify in their own behalf and whether a juror would hold that against defendants. Counsel's specificity helped to preserve the error for appellate review. The trial court was required to allow counsel to ask the jurors those and followup questions during voir dire and to discharge for cause a juror who indicated that he would be prejudiced by defendants not testifying. The trial court's proposed instructions could not cure that type of juror prejudice.


OUTCOME: The appeals court reversed more culpable defendant's convictions and sentences and remanded those charges for a new trial. The appeals court vacated the less culpable defendant's methamphetamine manufacturing, intent to manufacture, and receiving stolen property convictions and sentences. The appeals court reversed the less culpable defendant's convictions and sentences for paraphernalia and remanded that charge for a new trial.

 

193 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Lopez v. Commonwealth


2003-SC-0878-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


173 S.W.3d 905; 2005 Ky. LEXIS 327



October 20, 2005, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 10, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 2003-CA-1332. FAYETTE DISTRICT COURT NO. 03-XX-4.
Lopez v. Commonwealth, 2003 Ky. App. LEXIS 256 (Ky. Ct. App., Oct. 10, 2003)



DISPOSITION: REVERSING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A district court jury convicted defendant of operating a motor vehicle with alcohol concentration of or above 0.08, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 189A.010(1)(a). A circuit court reversed. The Court of Appeals (Kentucky) denied discretionary review. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court held that it was error to introduce a videotape of defendant's field sobriety test. Defendant sought review of the circuit court's decision with regards to a jury instruction. However, the Commonwealth did not file a cross motion with respect to the reversal or for discretionary review. Thus, the circuit court's reversal for a new trial because of the admission of the sobriety test was not an issue before the appellate court. The case was thus to be retried. The only issue was how to instruct the jury on retrial. The elements of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 189A.010(1)(a) were having a blood alcohol concentration of 0.08 or more and operating or being in control of a vehicle. These two elements needed to coincide. The trial court's instruction required the jury to find that defendant had a blood alcohol concentration of 0.08 or more at the time he was operating or in physical control of a motor vehicle. This instruction was proper, and the prosecutor should not have been allowed to tell the jury that defendant's blood alcohol concentration did not have to be 0.08 or more when he was operating his motor vehicle if it was at that level when the test was given.


OUTCOME: The circuit court was reversed and the appellate court held that the district court properly instructed the jury but erroneously failed to sustain the objections to the prosecutor's opening statement and closing argument. The case was remanded.

 

194 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Deno v. Commonwealth


2004-SC-000233-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


177 S.W.3d 753; 2005 Ky. LEXIS 302



September 22, 2005, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 22, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Deno v. Commonwealth, 2005 Ky. LEXIS 1038 (Ky., Dec. 22, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM JESSAMINE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE C. HUNTER DAUGHERTY, JUDGE. NO. 03-CR-00081.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of rape by the Jessamine Circuit Court (Kentucky). Defendant asserted that the trial court erred when it informed him he had no right to hybrid representation, held an inadequate hearing on his request for substitute counsel, admitted evidence regarding his refusal to voluntarily provide biological specimens, and refused to instruct the jury on sexual misconduct.


OVERVIEW: The victim accused defendant of having non-consensual sex with her while she was intoxicated. Defendant refused to give a DNA sample when initially asked by the police. A search warrant was obtained and his DNA matched that found on the victim. On the first day of trial, prior to the jury being selected, defendant requested that he be allowed to act as co-counsel was denied. The appellate court held that the trial court erred in denying that request. Defendant informed the judge of his dissatisfaction with his appointed attorney after motions in limine had been heard. His request was timely and unequivocal considering the circumstances under which the request was made. However, the trial court followed the correct procedure for addressing defendant's concerns with his representation. Thus, there was no error in the denial of substitute counsel. The admission of defendant's refusal to provide specimens was a violation of his rights under the Fourth Amendment and Ky. Const. § 10 as he had not been arrested. Because the victim was of majority age and defendant was of majority age, the refusal to instruct the jury on sexual misconduct was not erroneous.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the matter was remanded for a retrial.

 

195 of 1068 DOCUMENTS



Ky. Farm Bureau Mut. Ins. Co. v. Rodgers


2002-SC-1044-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


179 S.W.3d 815; 2005 Ky. LEXIS 294



September 22, 2005, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 19, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Ky. Farm Bureau Mut. Ins. Co. v. Rodgers, 2006 Ky. LEXIS 460 (Ky., Jan. 19, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 2001-CA-152 AND 2001-CA-206. LINCOLN CIRCUIT COURT NO. 98-CI-274.
Ky. Farm Bureau Mut. Ins. Co. v. Rodgers, 2003 Ky. LEXIS 131 (Ky., June 6, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insured sued defendant insurer alleging a violation of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 304.12-230, the Unfair Claims Settlement Practices Act (UCSPA). A jury awarded the insured $ 30,000.00 in compensatory damages and $ 1,000,000.00 in punitive damages. The trial court entered judgment accordingly and also awarded the insured attorney fees and costs. The Court of Appeals (Kentucky) affirmed. The insurer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The insured was injured in a car accident. The insurer made basic reparations benefits payments directly to the insured's medical providers, exhausting the limits on the insured's policy. The insurance company of the party at fault paid the insured the limits of that person's policy. When the insured demanded payment from the insurer of the underinsured motorists (UIM) coverage limits, the insurer only offered the insured a portion of that limit, deducting the sum of the money it had already paid and that received from the other insurance company. The issue before supreme court was whether the trial court erred in admitting "bad acts" evidence in violation of Ky. R. Evid. 404(b). The insurer's motion in limine to exclude the evidence at issue, the testimony of a party who had previously made a claim against the insurer, was overruled. The supreme court concluded that the testimony was erroneously admitted because the other action was not similar to the instant action. Among other things, the insurer was the liability insurer of the tort defendant in that action, rather than the UIM insurer. In addition, the court noted that the same adjuster was not involved in both cases.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Court of Appeals was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial.


 

196 of 1068 DOCUMENTS



Commonwealth Natural Res. & Envtl. Prot. Cabinet v. Kentec Coal Co.


2003-SC-000622-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


177 S.W.3d 718; 2005 Ky. LEXIS 303



September 22, 2005, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 22, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 2002-CA-001239. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT NO. 98-CI-00580 AND 98-CI-02002.
Kentec Coal Co. v. Commonwealth, 2003 Ky. App. LEXIS 179 (Ky. Ct. App., July 25, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Kentucky Court of Appeals reversed a ruling of the trial court and a decision of appellant state environmental cabinet and found that the state environmental cabinet's assessment of a penalty against appellee mining company permittee, without access to a subsequent formal hearing based solely on a permittee's inability to pay, was unreasonable, arbitrary, and unconstitutional. The state environmental cabinet appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mining company permittee held a surface mining permit. An individual began to build a house in the area covered by it. The state environmental cabinet noted a "third-party disturbance" on the site and ordered the mining company permittee to submit a permit revision explaining how the land use would be affected. The mining company permittee did not do so. It was then ordered to submit a revision by a certain date. It did not do so. The state environmental cabinet then issued a cessation order and, based on it, issued a "Notice of Proposed Assessment" for the mining company's violation of the state environmental cabinet's orders. Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 350.0301(5) and 405 Ky. Admin. Regs. 7:092, § 6 provided that corporations, such as the mining company permittee, could challenge the monetary assessment, but only if it prepaid the proposed assessment. Another regulation provided that an individual did not have to prepay the assessment in order to challenge it. The state environmental cabinet and the trial court both ruled against the mining company permittee. The appellate court reversed. On appeal, the state supreme court found the statute and regulation were unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment was affirmed and the case was remanded to the state environmental cabinet for a formal hearing.


 

197 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Commonwealth


2005-SC-0272-OA


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


171 S.W.3d 53; 2005 Ky. LEXIS 233



August 25, 2005, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication, September 15, 2005.
Later proceeding at Jones v. Commonwealth, 2007 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 543 (Ky. Ct. App., Sept. 28, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: IN SUPREME COURT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee brought an action against respondent employer, seeking review of a personnel action taken against him by the employer. The Circuit Court of Franklin County (Kentucky) transferred the case. The employee then brought an original action against the employer, pursuant to Ky. R. Civ. P. 76.36, to challenge the personnel action.


OVERVIEW: The employee was a former county pretrial services officer. The employer was the Kentucky Administrative Office of the Courts (AOC). Initially, the employee filed his petition for appeal in a circuit court. The circuit court found that, because the employer was the administrative arm of the Supreme Court of Kentucky, requests for review of its actions could only have been brought before that court. The court held that the AOC was removed from legislative authority. However, the policy was not to contest the propriety of legislation in the area of governance of the AOC to which the court could have acceded through a wholesome comity. Pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13B.140, a party wishing to appeal an AOC personnel action was allowed to file such appeal in either the Franklin Circuit Court or the circuit court of the county in which that party resided or operated a place of business. In reviewing the AOC's action, the circuit court was confined to the record unless there was fraud or misconduct, was not to substitute its judgment for that of the AOC as to the weight of the evidence on fact questions, and was limited to affirming the order or reversing it and remanding the action.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's order of transfer was vacated and the case was remanded.

 

198 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Leap


2004-SC-000138-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


179 S.W.3d 809; 2005 Ky. LEXIS 235



August 25, 2005, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 19, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Commonwealth v. Leap, 2006 Ky. LEXIS 442 (Ky., Jan. 19, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Leap v. Kentucky, 549 U.S. 878, 127 S. Ct. 363, 166 L. Ed. 2d 136, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 7105 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DISCRETIONARY REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. APPEAL FROM CAMPBELL CIRCUIT COURT. NO. 00-CR-00241.
Leap v. Commonwealth, 2004 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 211 (Ky. Ct. App., Jan. 23, 2004)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth of Kentucky sought review of a judgment from the Court of Appeals of Kentucky, which remanded the trial court's conviction of defendant for wanton endangerment and for being a persistent felony offender (PFO) for further findings by the trial court regarding vacatur of several of the convictions. Defendant was also convicted of assault.


OVERVIEW: The victim testified that she met defendant in a bar, and she went with him to another bar, where they drank more alcohol and smoked some pot. Defendant beat the victim savagely and repeatedly, and he left her naked on the side of a road. She suffered multiple fractures and other serious injuries. On the morning of the first trial, one charge was dismissed by the Commonwealth. A mistrial resulted due to a hung jury. At the retrial, defendant was tried on the former charges as well as on a new charge for wanton endangerment. Defendant was convicted and sentenced. On appeal, the Court of Appeals remanded the matter for the Commonwealth to rebut the "presumption of prosecutorial vindictiveness" associated with the late filing of the endangerment charge. On further review, the court found that the Court of Appeals erred. The court held that it would not extend the presumption of "prosecutorial vindictiveness," as enunciated in Pearce and Perry, to the pretrial setting. Accordingly, the fact of the mistrial and the addition of the endangerment charge did not lead to that presumption, and it was deemed appropriate in the circumstances. Defendant failed to prove actual vindictiveness.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the Court of Appeals and reinstated the judgment of the trial court.

Baptist Healthcare Sys. v. Miller


2003-SC-471-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


177 S.W.3d 676; 2005 Ky. LEXIS 236



August 25, 2005, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 22, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Baptist Healthcare Sys. v. Miller, 2005 Ky. LEXIS 1049 (Ky., Dec. 22, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 2002-CA-0083. FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT NO. 98-CI-02593.
Baptist Healthcare Sys. v. Miller, 2003 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1067 (Ky. Ct. App., May 23, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital challenged the judgment of the Kentucky Court of Appeals, which affirmed a trial court award in the amount of $ 100,100 in favor of appellee patient for injuries received as a result of negligence.


OVERVIEW: The patient had gone to the hospital to have blood drawn upon her doctor's order. The phlebotomist employed by the hospital placed a tourniquet on the patient's arm and left her without supervision for approximately 10 minutes. When the phlebotomist returned from answering a telephone call in another room, the patient's arm was swollen and had changed colors. The patient, who was 80 years old, experienced medical complications with her arm and sought treatment. After medical consultation, three physicians concluded that the patient was experiencing nerve problems with her right arm and specifically related her condition to the tourniquet incident. The hospital contended on appeal that at the time it moved for summary judgment, the patient had not named an expert to testify as to the standard of care of a phlebotomist and that it should have been granted summary judgment instead of the trial court permitting a continuance to allow the patient to identify such an expert. The court held that there was no abuse of the trial court discretion in continuing the case to allow the patient to identify an expert.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.


 

200 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Krahwinkel v. Commonwealth Aluminum Corp.


2003-SC-0708-DG AND 2004-SC-0219-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


2005 Ky. LEXIS 238



August 25, 2005, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Released for publication February 23, 2006
Substituted opinion at, Remanded by Krahwinkel v. Commonwealth Aluminum Corp., 2005 Ky. LEXIS 394 (Ky., Feb. 23, 2006)
Rehearing denied by, Request granted Krahwinkel v. Commonwealth Aluminum Corp., 2006 Ky. LEXIS 65 (Ky., Feb. 23, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW AND CROSS-REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 2002-CA-124 AND 2002-CA-193. HANCOCK CIRCUIT COURT. NO. 97-CI-4.
Commonwealth Aluminum Corp. v. Krahwinkel, 2004 Ky. LEXIS 138 (Ky., June 9, 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an employee of a fluid capture system seller, sought review of a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which vacated a jury award of damages to the employee in his negligence action against appellee fluid capture system purchaser, arising from a slip and fall that the employee had while on the purchaser's premises. The jury had found both parties at fault. The purchaser filed a cross-appeal from the Court of Appeals' judgment.


OVERVIEW: The fluid capture system purchaser contracted with the seller for the purchase and installation of a system in the purchaser's industrial plant. There was a large amount of oil and grease on the motor room floor, and the employee of the seller slipped and fell through a hole to the floor below, resulting in serious injury. The employee filed a workers' compensation (WC) claim against his employer, the seller, and he received benefits. He also filed a negligence action against the purchaser. The trial court instructed the jury that the purchaser had a duty to exercise ordinary care to maintain its business in a reasonably safe condition, rather than with the employee's requested negligence per se instruction. The jury found both parties at fault and awarded damages to the employee. The Court of Appeals vacated the jury verdict, finding that recovery under the WC claim precluded any further award. On further review, the court held that under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.700(1), those parts of the award for which recovery was already had in the WC proceedings were to be vacated. However, other aspects of the award which were not covered in the WC benefits could be retained.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the Court of Appeals with respect to the vacatur of the employee's judgment in its entirety. The court vacated those amounts awarded in the judgment that duplicated benefits awarded to the employee under his workers' compensation claim, including damages for permanent impairment, lost wages, and medical expenses.
